Buyu — Sales and Trade

10 min
Combining a Saleable and Unsaleable Item in One Contract
Ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on combining unsaleable item with saleable item

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combining a saleable and unsaleable item in one contract, and distinguish between the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
When a valid and invalid item are sold together, uncertainty in price voids the entire sale, but separate pricing saves the valid portion.

This lesson examines a classic case in Hanafi sales law: the effect of bundling a permissible object of sale with an impermissible one in a single contract. The matn declares the entire sale void, but the Sahibayn introduce a nuance: if prices are itemized, the valid sale stands. The dispute turns on the role of price uncertainty (jahalah). Understanding this clarifies the Hanafi approach to defective contracts.

Guided Path
1
State the base ruling
Read the matn: it states that combining a free person (hurr) and a slave (abd) or a slaughtered goat (shah dhabihah) and a dead goat (maytah) in one sale voids the entire transaction. Identify the ruling: the sale of both items is void (batil/fasid).
The free person and dead goat are not valid objects of sale (mabi'), so their sale never occurred.
2
Understand the reasoning
The commentary explains that because the invalid item cannot be sold, its inclusion creates uncertainty (jahalah) in the price of the valid item. Since the contract is unitary, the defect spreads, making the entire sale fasid.
Jahalah in price is a recognized cause of invalidity in Hanafi sales law.
3
Identify the Sahibayn's objection
The 'benefit' (faidah) from the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) states that if each item's price is stated separately, the jahalah is removed, so the sale of the valid item is valid, even within the same contract.
The Sahibayn focus on the presence of uncertainty rather than the mere inclusion of an invalid item.
4
Trace the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Imam Abu Hanifa, the entire contract must be rescinded; under the Sahibayn, if prices are separate, the valid item's sale stands, and only the invalid portion is void.
The dispute does not affect the rule that free persons and carrion cannot be sold.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text presents both views but does not give tarjih. In Hanafi fatwa, Abu Hanifa's view is generally relied upon, but the Sahibayn's view is applied when prices are clearly itemized in the contract.
Later Hanafi works (e.g., al-Hidayah) may explicitly prefer one view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جمع بین حر و عبد او شاة ذكية و ميتة بطل البيع فيهما [ ٩٠٢](٢١)
آزاد بیع ہی نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح مردہ بکری مبیع ہی نہیں ہے اس لئے ان کی بیع ہی نہیں ہوئی۔ اور عقد ایک ہے اس لئے اس کا اثر دوسری مبیع یعنی غلام اور ذبح شدہ بکری پر بھی پڑے گا اور ان کی بیع بھی نہیں ہوگی (۲) آزاد اور مردہ بکری کی بیع ن ہونے کی وجہ سے غلام اور ذبح شدہ بکری کی قیمت میں جہالت آگئی اس لئے غلام اور ذبح شدہ بکری کی بیع بھی نہیں ہوگی۔
اصول یہاں یہ اصول ہے کہ آزاد اور مردہ بکری کی بیع ہوئی ہی نہیں اس لئے ان کے اثر سے غلام اور ذبح شدہ بکری کی بیج بھی فاسد ہوگی۔ فائده صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ غلام کی قیمت الگ بیان کی ہو اور آزاد کی قیمت الگ بیان کی ہو تو غلام کی بیچ ہو جائے گی چاہے دونوں ایک عقد میں بکے ہوں۔
کیونکہ دونوں کی قیمت الگ الگ ہونے کی وجہ سے آزاد کی بیع نہیں ہوئی تو غلام کی قیمت میں جہالت نہیں رہی اس لئے غلام کی بیع فاسد نہیں ہوگی۔ اسی طرح ذبح شدہ بکری کی کی قیمت الگ بیان کی گئی ہو تو مردہ بکری کی بیع نہیں ہوئی تب بھی ذبح شدہ بکری کی قیمت میں جہالت نہیں رہی اس لئے ذبح شدہ بکری کی بیچ ہا جائے گی۔ ت ذكية : ذبح کی ہوئی۔
Combining a free person and a slave or a slaughtered goat and a dead goat, the sale of both is void. [Commentary:] The free person is not a valid object of sale. Similarly, the dead goat is not a valid object of sale. Therefore their sale did not occur. And the contract is one, so its effect falls on the other object of sale, i.e., the slave and the slaughtered goat, and their sale also does not take place. (2) Because the sale of the free person and the dead goat did not occur, ignorance (jahalah) arose in the price of the slave and the slaughtered goat, so their sale also does not take place. The principle here is that the sale of the free person and the dead goat never occurred, so due to their effect, the sale of the slave and the slaughtered goat becomes invalid (fasid). Benefit: Sahibayn say: If the price of the slave is stated separately and the price of the free person is stated separately, then the sale of the slave will be valid, even if both are sold in one contract. Because due to the prices being separate, the sale of the free person did not occur, so there is no ignorance in the price of the slave, therefore the sale of the slave is not invalid. Similarly, if the price of the slaughtered goat is stated separately, then the sale of the dead goat did not occur, still there is no ignorance in the price of the slaughtered goat, so the sale of the slaughtered goat will be valid. (tadhkiyah: slaughtered)
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This is a ruling from the Book of Sales, presented with a subsequent intra-Hanafi dispute. The matn states that if one combines a free person (who cannot be sold) with a slave, or a slaughtered goat (valid) with a dead goat (invalid), in a single sale contract, the entire sale is void. The commentary explains that the unsaleable items never formed a valid sale, and because the contract is unitary, the invalidity spreads to the saleable items due to uncertainty (jahalah) in the price allocation. The commentator then provides a 'benefit' (faidah) from the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani): if each item's price is stated separately, the uncertainty is removed, so the sale of the valid item is valid. This shows that the invalidity in such cases stems from price ignorance, not from the contract itself.

Key Terms
حر (hurr): A free person; not a valid object of sale in Islamic law.
عبد (abd): A slave; a valid object of sale.
شاة ذكية (shah dhabihah): A slaughtered goat; a valid object of sale.
ميتة (maytah): A dead animal (carrion); not a valid object of sale.
بطل البيع (batala al-bay'): The sale is void; here meaning fasid (invalid) due to jahalah.
جاهلة (jahalah): Ignorance or uncertainty in the price, leading to invalidity of the sale.
صاحبين (Sahibayn): Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two main disciples of Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, what condition allows the sale of the valid item to be valid when combined with an invalid item in one contract?
A) The buyer must be aware of the invalid item.
B) The prices of each item must be stated separately.
C) The invalid item must be returned before payment.
D) The contract must be witnessed.

Key Takeaway
In a combined sale of valid and invalid items, price uncertainty (jahalah) voids the entire contract, but separate pricing per item preserves the valid portion according to the Sahibayn.

Combining a Slave and a Mudabbar in One Sale: Ruling and Proof
Ruling on the validity of a slave sale when bundled with a mudabbar or another's slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling a slave when bundled with a mudabbar or another's property and apply the principle of apportioned price.

Core Idea
A slave sold with a mudabbar is valid with a share of the price, because the mudabbar is saleable property.

This passage addresses a nuanced sales scenario: when a seller combines two items in one contract, but one of them cannot be sold for some reason (e.g., the mudabbar's sale fails, or the other item belongs to someone else). The Hanafi school, relying on a hadith that the Prophet ﷺ actually sold a mudabbar, holds that the mudabbar is valid property. Hence, the contract is not void; the valid item (the slave) stands, and the price is apportioned according to its value. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof, and the underlying principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
The passage presents two scenarios: (1) combining one's own slave with a mudabbar, and (2) combining one's own slave with another person's slave. Both are treated alike.
The mudabbar is a slave whose manumission is tied to the master's death; it is property in the Hanafi school.
2
State the ruling for each case
The ruling is that the sale of the (valid) slave is valid (sahih) for his share of the price. The mudabbar or another's slave does not pass, but their failure does not void the contract.
The share is determined by the proportion of the total price corresponding to the slave's value.
3
Locate the hadith proof
The author cites a hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari: 'The Prophet sold a mudabbar.' This establishes that the mudabbar is legally property (mal), making it a valid object of sale.
The hadith is ahad (single-chain) but accepted in rulings.
4
Extract the underlying principle
The principle is: if two items are sold together and both are legally property, the contract covers both. If one fails for an external reason, the other remains valid with an apportioned price.
This principle applies to any sale where one item's transfer is invalidated after the contract.
5
Apply the principle to the given examples
In example 1: slave and mudabbar worth 2000 total, slave's value 1000 → slave's sale valid for 1000. In example 2: one's own slave with another's slave → own slave's share is due from buyer.
The other's slave fails due to lack of ownership, not because it is not property.

Source Text

ومن جمع بين عبد ومدبر او بين عبده وعبد غيره صح البيع فى العبد بحصته من الثمن.
کسی نے غلام اور مدبر کوجمع کیا یا اپنے غلا اور غیر کے غلام کو بچ میں جمع کیا تو غلام میں ہی صحیح ہوئی اس کی قیمت کے حصے کے ساتھ۔
انا غلام اور مدبر غلام دونوں کو ایک بیچ میں جمع کر دیا۔ یا اپنے غلام کو اور دوسرے کے غلام کو بغیر اس کی اجازت کے ایک بیع میں جمع کر دیا تو مدبر کی بیچ تو نہیں ہوگی لیکن خالص غلام کی بیچ ہو جائے گی۔ اور جو قیمت اس کے حصے کی ہوگی وہ لازم ہوگی۔ مثلا دو ہزار کے غلام اور مدبر تھے تو خالص غلام کی قیمت ایک ہزار رہ گئی تو ایک ہزار لازم ہوں گے۔ اسی طرح دوسرے کا غلام اس کی اجازت کے بغیر بیج میں داخل نہیں ہوگا۔ لیکن اپنے غلام کی بیچ ہو جائے گی۔ اور جو اس کے حصے کی قیمت ہے وہ مشتری پر لازم ہوگی۔ مد بر کسی نہ کسی امام کے نزدیک غلام کی طرح بکنے کے قابل ہے اس لئے وہ مال ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے عن جابر قال باع النبی اے المدبر (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب بیع المد بر ص ۲۹۷ نمبر ۲۲۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مر بر غلام بکنے کے قابل ہے۔ اس لئے اس کو خالص غلام کے ساتھ ملایا تو بیع ہو گئی۔ اب بعد میں مدبر کی بیع ن ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کی قیمت الگ ہوگی اور کم ہوگی۔ اس لئے غلام کی بیچ ہو گئی۔ یہی حال اپنے غلام اور دوسرے غلام کو ملانے کا ہے۔
اصول یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ مبیع کے ساتھ دوسری بیع مال ہے اور بکنے کے قابل ہے۔ اس لئے دونوں مبیع کی لیکن کسی وجہ سے دوسری طبیع ن بک سکی تو پہلی مبیع بیع میں داخل ہوگی۔ اور اس کی قیمت اس کے حصے کے مطابق لازم ہوگی ۔
حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت جابر فرماتے ہیں کہ آپ نے مد بر غلام کو بیچا ہے۔
And whoever combines a slave and a mudabbar, or his own slave and another's slave, the sale of the slave is valid for his share of the price. [Commentary:] If someone combines a slave and a mudabbar, or his own slave and another's slave without his permission in one sale, then the mudabbar's sale does not occur, but the pure slave's sale will be valid. And whatever price corresponds to his share will be due. For example, if the slave and mudabbar were worth 2000, and the pure slave's share is 1000, then 1000 is due. Similarly, another's slave without his permission will not be included in the sale, but one's own slave's sale will be valid, and the price of his share is due from the buyer. The mudabbar, according to some imams, is fit to be sold like a slave, so it is property. There is a hadith from Jabir: 'The Prophet sold a mudabbar' (Bukhari, Book of Sales, Chapter on Selling Mudabbar, no. 223). From this hadith it is known that a mudabbar slave is fit to be sold. Therefore, when he is combined with a pure slave, the sale occurred. Now, because the mudabbar's sale did not take place, his price will be separate and will be reduced, so the slave's sale took place. The same applies to combining one's own slave with another's slave. The principle: This issue is based on the principle that if the other item is property and fit to be sold, then both are objects of sale, but if for some reason the other cannot be sold, the first item remains in the sale and its price is due according to its share.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage presents a second ruling: if a slave is combined with a mudabbar (a slave whose emancipation is tied to the master's death) or with another person's slave without permission in a single sale contract, the sale of the (first) slave is valid for his share of the price. The commentary explains that the mudabbar's sale fails, but since the mudabbar is itself a valid property (as proven by the hadith of Jabir that the Prophet sold a mudabbar), the contract initially covers both. When the second item's sale fails, the first remains valid and the price is apportioned. An example is given: if total price is 2000 and the slave's share is 1000, then 1000 is due. The same applies to the case of one's own slave with another's slave: the other's sale fails (due to lack of ownership), but one's own slave is valid. The principle is that if the accompanying item is itself valid property, its failure does not invalidate the other item's sale; the price is determined proportionally.

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whose manumission is promised upon the master's death; considered property and salable.
حصتہ من الثمن (hissatuhu min al-thaman): His share of the price, i.e., the proportion of the total price corresponding to the slave's value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The Quranic verse on sales
B) The hadith of Jabir that the Prophet sold a mudabbar
C) Consensus of the Sahaba
D) Analogy with a regular slave

Key Takeaway
When a slave is sold together with a mudabbar, the slave's sale remains valid with its share of the price, because the mudabbar is legally property as proven by the hadith.

Ruling on Najsh and Contract Validity
Prohibition of najsh and effect on sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on najsh, identify the evidence, and explain why the sale contract remains valid despite the prohibition.

Core Idea
Najsh is prohibited but the sale stands because the contract core is sound.

This lesson examines a classic sales ethics issue: a buyer artificially inflating the price to deceive others. We first define najsh, then explore the hadith prohibiting it, and finally understand the Hanafi position that the sinful act does not nullify the contract. This distinction between the moral ruling on the act and the validity of the contract is a key feature of Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Identify the act being discussed: najsh (bidding without intention to buy). Determine the hukm level from the text: makruh (disliked/prohibited).
The commentary specifies that it is makruh due to harm and prophetic prohibition.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence cited: the hadith of Ibn Umar, 'The Prophet forbade najsh.' Classify it as Sunnah ahad (zanni al-thubut) and note its sources (Bukhari, Muslim, Tirmidhi).
The dalil is explicitly quoted in the Arabic passage.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith proves the ruling. The explicit prohibition (nahi) indicates the act is prohibited. The principle that the contract's validity depends on its core elements (sulb al-'aqd) means the external sinful act does not invalidate the exchange.
Hanafi usul: nahi does not necessarily invalidate the contract unless the prohibition targets an essential part of the contract.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Recognize that some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i or Malikis in one view) may consider the sale null if the bidder has no intent to buy. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the prohibition of the act and the validity of the contract.
The text mentions the sale is valid 'because there is no defect in the contract itself', implying a nuanced position.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The operative ruling for fatwa: najsh is makruh tahrimi (prohibited) but the resulting sale is valid. This is based on the clear hadith and the principle of sulb al-'aqd.
The Hanafi position is consistent with the majority of Hanafi authorities.

Source Text

ونهى رسول الله عن النجش
نجش کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ خود کوخرید نانہیں ہے لیکن قیمت لگا کر خواہ مخواہ اس کی قیمت بڑھا رہا ہے تا کہ دوسرا آدمی مہنگا خریدے۔ اس کو
ولالی کرنا کہتے ہیں ایسا کرنا مکروہ ہے۔
(۱) اس میں دوسرے کو نقصان دیتا ہے اس لئے مکروہ ہے (۲) حدیث میں ایسا کرنے سے منع فرمایا ہے عن ابن عمر قال نھی النبي الله عن النجش (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب النجش و من قال لا يجوز ذلک البیع ص ۲۸۷ نمبر ۲۱۴۲ ر مسلم شریف ، باب تحریم پیچ الرجل على بيع احيه وسومه على سومه وتحريم النخش وتحريم التصریۃ ص ۳ نمبر ۱۵۱۶ر ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی کراہیتہ النجش ص ۲۴۴ نمبر ۱۳۰۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ دلالی کرنا ممنوع ہے تا ہم بیچ ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ صلب عقد میں خامی نہیں ہے۔
And the Messenger of Allah forbade najsh. Najsh means that a person does not intend to buy but bids up the price unnecessarily to make another person buy expensive. This is called 'dallali' (brokering). Doing so is makruh (disliked). (1) It harms others, so it is makruh. (2) The hadith forbids it. From Ibn Umar: The Prophet forbade najsh (Bukhari, Muslim, Tirmidhi). From this hadith it is understood that najsh is prohibited, nevertheless the sale will be valid because there is no defect in the contract itself.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage presents the prohibition of najsh, defined as a person who does not intend to buy but artificially raises the price during an auction or negotiation to trick another into paying more. The commentary explains that this act is makruh (disliked, likely makruh tahrimi) for two reasons: it harms the actual buyer, and it is explicitly forbidden by the hadith of Ibn Umar (and others). However, despite the prohibition, the resulting sale contract itself is valid because the defect (najsh) does not affect the core elements (offer and acceptance, price, object). The sale is not void; only the act of najsh is sinful.

Key Terms
نجش (najsh): A person who has no intention to buy but bids up the price to deceive others into paying more.
مكروه (makruh): Disliked; here likely makruh tahrimi (prohibited)
صلب عقد (sulb al-'aqd): The core/essence of the contract (offer, acceptance, consideration).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The sale becomes void (batil).
B) The sale is valid but the act is prohibited.
C) The sale is suspended until the buyer confirms.
D) The sale is valid only if the real buyer consents.

Key Takeaway
Najsh is a prohibited act, but the resulting sale contract remains valid because the prohibition does not affect the core contractual elements.

The Conditional Prohibition of Bidding Over Another's Bid
Ruling on bidding over another's bid with proof and exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bidding over another's bid, identify the condition of inclination, and distinguish between prohibited and permissible scenarios using the two hadiths.

Core Idea
Bidding over another's bid is prohibited only when the first bidder is inclined; open auctions remain permissible.

This lesson tackles a common practical issue in sales: is it allowed to outbid someone who is already negotiating? The Hanafi school, relying on clear prophetic hadiths, gives a nuanced answer. The prohibition is not absolute but conditional on the first bidder's inclination to finalize the purchase. Understanding this condition prevents harm and guides proper conduct in markets and auctions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Ruling
The act is 'bidding over a bid' (al-sawm 'ala sawm) – raising the price after someone else has already made an offer. State the general Hanafi ruling: it is makruh tahrimi if the first bidder is inclined to buy, otherwise permissible.
The ruling is not about the validity of the sale but about the sinfulness of the action.
2
Examine the Primary Hadith (Abu Hurairah)
The hadith explicitly forbids a man to 'sell over his brother's sale' or 'bid over his bid.' This establishes a general prohibition. Note that the hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim, accepted as sound.
The phrase 'his brother' indicates the moral obligation not to harm another Muslim.
3
Recognize the Exception: The Auction Hadith (Anas)
The hadith of Anas shows the Prophet conducting an auction (bay' al-man yazid) where multiple bids were made openly. The Prophet encouraged higher bids and sold to the highest bidder. This indicates that bidding over another's bid is allowed when no one is yet inclined to finalize.
The two hadiths together show the rule and its exception.
4
Determine the Condition: Inclination
The key factor is whether the first bidder has become 'inclined' (close to accepting). If yes, bidding over him is prohibited to prevent harm. If not, it is permissible because the negotiation is still open.
Inclination is judged by outward signs, such as reaching a tentative agreement or being about to finalize.
5
Apply to Contemporary Scenarios
Practice by applying the rule: in a private negotiation where the buyer is about to say 'yes', do not outbid. In a public auction with active bidding and no one committed, bidding over is allowed.
The same principle applies to online auctions with ongoing bids.

Source Text

وعن السوم على سوم
دوسرا آدمی بیع کے لئے بھاؤ کر رہا ہے۔ اب وہ خریدنے کے قریب ہے کہ آپ نے بھاؤ کر دیا یہ مکروہ ہے۔ پہلے بھاؤ کرنے والے کو متوحش کرتا ہے اور نقصان دیتا ہے اس لئے مکروہ ہے (۲) حدیث میں ایسا کرنے سے منع فرمایا گیا ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة قال نهى رسول الله الله الله ان يبيع حاضر لباد ولا تناجشوا ولا يبيع الرجل على بيع اخيه (ب) ( بخاری شریف ، باب لابی علی بیع احیہ ولا یسوم علی سوم احیه حتی یا ذن له او ترک ص ۲۸۷ نمبر ۲۱۴۰ مسلم شریف ، باب تحریم بیع الرجل علی بیج اخیہ وسومه علی سومہ ص ۳ نمبر ۱۵۱۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ کوئی بھاؤ کر رہا ہو اور مائل ہو چکا ہو تو اس پر بھاؤ کرنا مکروہ ہے۔ اگر ابھی مائل نہ ہوا ہو تو دوسرا آدمی بھاؤ کر سکتا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ یہ بیع من یزید ہے۔ اور حدیث میں اس کی اجازت ہے۔ عن انس بن مالک ان رسول الله باع حلسا وقدحا وقال من يشترى هذا الحلس والقدح فقال رجل اخذ تهما بدرهم فقال النبي الا الله من يزيد على درهم ؟ من يزيد علی درهم ؟ فاعطاه رجل در همین فباعهما منه (ج) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی بیع من یزید ص ۲۳۰ نمبر ۱۲۱۸) اس حدیث میں آپ نے بیع من یزید کی اور کئی آدمیوں نے بھاؤ پر بھاؤ کئے لیکن چونکہ کوئی آدمی بالکل خرید لینے پر مائل نہیں تھا اس لئے دوسرے کے لئے بھاؤ کرنا جائز تھا۔
And forbidding bidding over a bid. Another person is bidding to buy. He is about to buy; then you come and bid. This is makruh. It harms the first bidder and causes him to withdraw, so it is makruh. (2) The hadith forbids it: Abu Hurairah reported the Prophet forbade that a townsman sell for a Bedouin, do najsh, and that a man sell over his brother's sale or bid over his brother's bid (Bukhari, Muslim). From this hadith it is understood that if someone is bidding and is inclined to buy, then bidding over him is makruh. But if he is not yet inclined, then another person may bid, because this is a regular auction (bay' al-man yazid). And there is a hadith of Anas ibn Malik that the Prophet sold a blanket and a bowl, and said 'Who will buy this blanket and bowl?' A man said 'I take them for one dirham.' The Prophet said 'Who will give more than one dirham? Who will give more than one dirham?' A man gave him two dirhams, so he sold them to him (Tirmidhi). In this hadith, the Prophet conducted an auction, and several people bid over each other, but since no one was completely inclined to buy (i.e., the sale was not finalized), it was permissible for others to bid.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage addresses the prohibition of bidding over another person's bid (al-sawm 'ala sawm). The commentary explains that if a person is already bidding and is inclined (close to buying), then another person coming and offering a higher price is makruh (disliked/prohibited) because it harms the first bidder. This is supported by the hadith of Abu Hurairah. However, the text provides an important exception: if the first bidder is not yet inclined (i.e., the sale is not imminent, such as in an open auction where multiple bidders compete freely), then bidding over his bid is permissible. This is evidenced by the hadith of Anas where the Prophet conducted an auction (bay' al-man yazid) and multiple people bid without any being 'inclined' to finalize. Thus, the prohibition applies only when the first bidder is at the point of commitment, not in general auctions.

Key Terms
سوم (sawm): Bidding or offering a price for an item.
سوم على سوم (sawm 'ala sawm): Bidding over another person's existing bid.
بیع من یزید (bay' al-man yazid): Auction; sale to the highest bidder.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In an open auction (bay' al-man yazid), is it permissible for a new person to bid after someone else has placed a bid?
A) Yes, because the first bidder is not yet committed.
B) No, it is always prohibited.
C) Only if the auctioneer allows it.
D) It is makruh but the sale is valid.

Key Takeaway
Bidding over another's bid is prohibited only when the first bidder is inclined to buy; otherwise, as in open auctions, it is permissible – a ruling derived from harmonizing the two prophetic hadiths.

Ruling on Sale of Mudabbar vs. Free Person
Explains why a mudabbar's sale is valid while a free person's sale is invalid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the legal difference in the validity of a sale when the subject is a mudabbar slave versus a free person, and explain the basis for the distinction.

Core Idea
A mudabbar can be sold because he is part of the estate; a free person cannot be sold because he is not property.

In Hanafi sales law, the subject matter must be owned and transferable. This passage compares two cases: one involving a free person (who cannot be sold) and another involving a mudabbar slave (who can be sold due to his status as part of the estate). Understanding this distinction is crucial for grasping the concepts of ownership and asset liquidity in inheritance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
The passage contrasts Issue 20 (free person sold with a slave) with the current case (mudabbar sold).
The free person's sale is invalid from the start.
2
State the ruling for each
The free person's sale is batil (void); the mudabbar's sale is sahih (valid).
Invalid sale never occurred.
3
Identify the basis
A free person cannot be sold because he is not property; a mudabbar is part of the estate and thus can be sold for debt settlement.
The mudabbar's status as mal (asset) is key.
4
Contrast the legal effects
In Issue 20, the entire contract was fasid (corrupt); here, the mudabbar's sale is valid, and proceeds are divided.
Shows the importance of subject matter.
5
Summarize the principle
Anything that is not owned cannot be sold; anything that is part of the estate can be sold to fulfill obligations.
Applies to all assets.

Source Text

مسئلہ نمبر ۲۰ کا اصول یہ تھا کہ از سر نو آزاد کی بیع ہی نہیں ہوئی تھی اس لئے اس کے ساتھ غلام کی بیع فاسد ہوئی۔ اور یہاں یہ ہے کہ مد برمن وجہ مال ہونے کی وجہ سے بیچ ہوگئی اور بعد میں قیمت کی تقسیم ہوئی۔
The principle of issue number 20 was that from the beginning the sale of a free person had not occurred, therefore the sale of the slave with him was invalid. And here it is that the mudabbar, due to being part of the estate, was sold and later the price was divided.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is a comparative ruling. It distinguishes between a previous case (issue 20) where a free person was sold along with a slave. Since the sale of a free person is fundamentally invalid, the entire contract was void. In the current case, the mudabbar slave is sold because he is part of the deceased's estate, and the sale is valid, with the proceeds divided among heirs.

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who has been promised freedom upon the master's death

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why was the mudabbar's sale valid while the previous case of selling a free person was not?
A) Because the free person was not actually sold
B) Because the mudabbar is part of the estate
C) Because the slave was sold separately
D) Because the master gave permission

Key Takeaway
The key distinction: a mudabbar is part of the estate and can be sold for debt settlement, while a free person cannot be sold at all.

Prohibition of Najsh and Bidding Over Another's Bid
States two prohibitions with hadith evidence and legal rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on najsh and bidding over another's bid, distinguish between permissible and impermissible bidding, and explain why the sale remains valid despite the prohibition.

Core Idea
Najsh and bidding over a committed bid are makruh; the sale is valid because the contract's core is sound.

The Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited two deceptive practices in sales: najsh (artificially inflating price) and bidding over another person's bid when the buyer is committed. In this lesson, we examine the hadith evidence, the reasoning behind the prohibition, and the Hanafi ruling that the sale remains valid despite the act being makruh. You will also learn the exception where competitive bidding is allowed, as demonstrated by the Prophet's own auction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two prohibited practices
Read the passage and clearly define najsh (pretending to buy to inflate price) and bidding over another's bid (offering a higher price when the first buyer is already inclined to purchase).
2
Examine the hadith evidence
For najsh, the hadith from Ibn Umar (naha an-najsh). For bidding over a bid, the hadith from Abu Huraira (nahaa an yabi'u rajulun 'ala bay'i akhih). Note that these are ahad hadiths, so they indicate prohibition but not certainty in transmission.
The prohibition is explicit (نهى), indicating the act is makruh.
3
Understand the ruling: makruh, not batil
Despite the prohibition, the sale contract remains valid because the pillars (ijab, qabul, subject matter, price) are sound. The prohibition targets the deceptive behavior, not the contract itself.
4
Identify the exception: permissible bidding
The passage explains that if the first bidder is not yet committed (not mā'il), another may bid. This is supported by the Prophet's auction (bay' man yazid) where multiple bids were allowed.
The auction hadith from Anas shows multiple bids without harm.

Source Text

903 (22) And the Messenger of Allah (may Allah bless him) prohibited najsh. [904] (23) And [he prohibited] bidding over a bid. ... (then explanations and hadiths) ...
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is a double ruling with proof. It covers two prohibitions: najsh (artificially inflating price) and bidding over someone else's bid. Both are makruh (disliked) due to causing harm, but the contracts remain valid because the core elements are sound. The hadith for najsh is from Ibn Umar, and for bidding over another's bid from Abu Huraira. The exception is when the first bidder is not committed, as in the auction of the Prophet (peace be upon him) where bidding was allowed. The footnote explains the hadiths.

Key Terms
النجش (al-najsh): Artificially inflating the price of an item by pretending to buy it without intending to purchase
السوم على سوم (al-soum 'ala soum): Bidding or offering a price over another person's bid when that person is already inclined to buy
بیع من یزید (bay' man yazid): Auction-style sale where bids are increased

Key Takeaway
Najsh and bidding over a committed bid are makruh; the sale remains valid; bidding is allowed when the first party is not committed.

Prohibition of Townsman Selling to Villager (Bay' al-Hadir lil-Badi)
Prohibits townsman selling essential goods to villager when townspeople need them

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bay' al-hadir lil-badi and apply the condition that determines its permissibility.

Core Idea
A townsman may only sell to a villager if it does not harm the townspeople who have a greater right.

This lesson examines a classical Hanafi ruling that protects local communities from exploitation during shortages. The Prophet ﷺ prohibited townsmen from selling essential goods to visiting villagers when townspeople are in need. You will learn the precise conditions that trigger this prohibition and when it becomes permissible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is a townsman (hadir) selling goods to a villager (badi). The ruling is that it is makruh if townspeople are in need of those goods.
The text explicitly says 'makruh' (مکروہ), not haram.
2
Locate the Dalil
The proof is the hadith narrated by Abu Hurairah: 'The Prophet ﷺ prohibited the townsman from selling for the villager.' Also the saying of Ibn Abbas explaining that it means the townsman should not act as a middleman (samsar).
The hadith is in Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The hadith's general prohibition indicates that the act is disapproved. The Hanafi school interprets it as makruh tanzihi (disliked) rather than haram, because the harm is not absolute and can be mitigated by the condition of need.
The prohibition is tied to harm; when harm is absent, the ruling changes.
4
Apply the Condition
The text adds a conditional exception: if townspeople do not need the goods, the townsman may sell to the villager. This condition determines the ruling.
The condition is essential: the prohibition applies only when townspeople are in need.
5
Note the Thamarah (Practical Effect)
The practical effect is that a town trader must prioritize local needs over external buyers during shortages. If there is no shortage, trade with villagers is permissible.
This ruling prevents exploitation and ensures community welfare.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۹۰۶] (۲۵) اور آپ نے منع فرمایا شہر والوں کی بیچ دیہات والوں سے۔
شہر والوں کو مثلا غلوں کی سخت ضرورت ہے اس کے باوجود تاجر دیہات سے آنے والے لوگوں سے زیادہ قیمت میں غلہ بیچ رہے ہیں تو یہ مکروہ ہے۔ کیونکہ اس سے شہر والوں کو نقصان ہوگا ۔ وہ محتاج ہیں اور ان کا زیادہ حق ہے (۲) حدیث میں منع فرمایا گیا ہے عن ابی هر بر قال نهى النبي الله عن التلقى وان يبيع حاضر لباد (ب) ( بخاری شریف ، باب النھی عن تلقی الرکبان ص ۲۸۹ نمبر ۲۱۶۲ ر مسلم شریف، باب تحریم بیع الحاضر للمبادی ص ۴ نمبر ۱۵۲۰) اس حدیث میں منع فرمایا گیا ہے کہ شہر والے دیہات والوں سے ضرورت کے وقت سامان فروخت کرے۔ اور شہر والوں کو ضرورت نہ ہو تو دیہات والوں سے بیچ سکتا ہے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے سالت ابن عباس ما معنى قوله لا يبيعن حاضر لباد؟ قال لا يكون له سمسار (ج) (بخاری شریف، باب النھی عن تلقی الرکبان ص ۲۸۹ نمبر ۱۲۱۶۳ مسلم شریف، باب حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے تلقی بالجلب سے روکا اور اس سے بھی کہ شہر والے دیہات والے سے بیچے (ب) آپ نے تلقی بالجلب سے روکا اور اس سے بھی کہ شہر والے دیہات والے سے نیچے (ج) حضرت عبداللہ بن عباس سے لا یعن حاضر لباد کا مطلب پوچھا تو فرمایا کہ ان کے لئے دلال نہ بنے ہسمسار دلال کو کہتے ہیں۔
[906 (25) And the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited the townsman selling to the villager. If townspeople are in dire need of grain, and traders sell to villagers at high prices, it is makruh because it harms the needy townspeople who have more right. The hadith prohibits it. The ruling is that if townspeople do not need the goods, a townsman may sell to a villager. The evidence is the saying of Ibn Abbas: 'It means he should not be a middleman for them.'
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on bay' al-hadir lil-badi. It prohibits townsmen from selling essential goods to villagers when townspeople are in need, as it causes harm and exploitation. The hadith is cited, and a qualification is added: if townspeople are not in need, it is permissible. The commentary from Ibn Abbas explains that the prohibition means the townsman should not act as a middleman exploiting the villager.

Key Terms
بيع الحاضر للبادي (bay' al-hadir lil-badi): A townsman selling goods to a villager, especially when townspeople are in need of those goods
سمسار (samsar): Middleman or broker who facilitates sales

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is it permissible for a townsman to sell to a villager?
A) When the villager offers a higher price
B) When the townspeople are not in need of the goods
C) When the sale is conducted outside the city
D) When the villager is a relative

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on bay' al-hadir lil-badi is that it is makruh only when townspeople are in need; otherwise it is permissible.

The Ruling of Talaqqi al-Jalab
Ruling on talaqqi al-jalab with proof and qualification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on talaqqi al-jalab, explain the reasons for its prohibition, and identify the condition under which it becomes permissible.

Core Idea
Meeting caravans before market is prohibited when it harms merchants or townspeople; if no harm, it is allowed.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on talaqqi al-jalab—the practice of going out to meet incoming merchants before they reach the market to buy their goods cheaply. The text presents the prohibition based on a prophetic hadith and provides a nuanced analysis: the sale is disliked (makruh tahrimi) when it causes harm, but permissible when no harm occurs. We will unpack the evidence, the reasoning, and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what the initial hukm is. The act is talaqqi al-jalab (meeting caravans). The text states it is makruh (disliked), but with qualification.
The ruling is not absolute; it depends on the presence of harm.
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the proof cited. The author cites the hadith 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited talaqqi and that a townsman sell for a Bedouin.'
This is a hadith from Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith proves the ruling. The explicit prohibition (نهى) indicates the act is prohibited, which in Hanafi usul implies makruh tahrimi unless specified otherwise.
The prohibition is taken seriously but the Hanafi school allows istihsan to override based on absence of harm.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Observe that the Shafi'i school also considers it prohibited based on the same hadith, but some allow if no harm. The Hanafi school uniquely qualifies the ruling.
The difference stems from the role of the underlying cause ('illa) of harm.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Understand the relied-upon position: talaqqi al-jalab is makruh tahrimi when it causes harm or deception; otherwise permissible. This is based on the principle of preventing harm and the hadith of no harm (la darar).
The mufta bihi position balances the textual prohibition with the objective of preventing harm.

Other than it [905] (24) And from meeting the caravans [906] (25) And from the townsman selling for the Bedouin. And causing harm to someone or frightening them is disliked. The hadith 'La darar wa la dirar' has passed. Al-sawm: making a price. [1905] (24) And he prohibited meeting merchants. Talaqqi means to go forward and meet someone. And jalab means to pull or attract profit. Here talaqqi al-jalab means that when merchants come from outside to sell goods, one goes out of the city to meet them and buys all the goods cheaply, so that later he sells the goods to the townspeople at a higher price. This is called talaqqi al-jalab. It is disliked because: (1) Sometimes the merchant is deceived by not being informed of the correct market price, and the buyer buys the goods cheaply. This harms the merchants, so it is disliked. (2) Sometimes the townspeople have a dire need for grain, and the grain brought from outside is bought by a few specific traders, so the townspeople will not get grain or will get it very expensive. In this case, the townspeople are harmed, so talaqqi al-jalab is disliked. (3) The hadith prohibits talaqqi al-jalab: 'From Abu Hurairah (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited talaqqi and that a townsman sell for a Bedouin.' (Bukhari, Bab al-Nahy an Talaqqi al-Rukban, p. 289, no. 2162; Muslim, Bab Tahrim Talaqqi al-Jalab, p. no. 1519). This hadith shows that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited talaqqi al-jalab. Question: If the townspeople are harmed, this sale is disliked. But if the townspeople do not need this grain and the incoming caravan is not deceived regarding the price, then talaqqi al-jalab is not disliked.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school concerning the prohibition of talaqqi al-jalab (meeting caravans). The author first states the ruling: the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited meeting caravans before they reach the market. He then provides a detailed explanation of the practice: it involves going out of the city to meet incoming merchants and buying all their goods cheaply, then reselling at a higher price in the city. The author lists three reasons for the prohibition: (1) it defrauds the merchant by concealing the true market price; (2) it harms the townspeople by hoarding essential goods, causing scarcity and higher prices; (3) the direct prohibition from the Prophet (peace be upon him) in the hadith of Abu Hurairah. Importantly, the author qualifies the ruling: if there is no harm to the townspeople and no deception of the merchant, then the practice is not disliked. This is a typical Hanafi approach of considering the underlying cause ('illa) of harm.

Key Terms
تلقي الجلب (talaqqī al-jalab): Going out to meet incoming merchants before they reach the market to buy their goods at a low price, often to resell at a profit.
مكروه (makrūh): An act that is disliked and whose commission is sinful, but it does not invalidate the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi text, which of the following is a condition that makes talaqqi al-jalab not disliked?
A) The merchant is informed of the market price and the townspeople do not need the goods.
B) The buyer is a townsman and the seller is a Bedouin.
C) The goods are perishable and must be sold quickly.
D) The transaction takes place within the city limits.

Key Takeaway
Talaqqi al-jalab is not inherently prohibited; its ruling depends on the presence of harm to the merchant or the townspeople.

Prohibition of Townsman Selling for Bedouin (Bay' al-Hadhir lil-Badi)
Explaining the ruling and reasons for prohibiting a townsman selling on behalf of a Bedouin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bay' al-hadhir lil-badi and identify the condition (need of townspeople) that makes it prohibited.

Core Idea
Bay' al-hadhir lil-badi is prohibited only when it harms the needy townspeople.

This lesson explains a specific prohibition in sales: a townsman selling on behalf of a villager (or acting as a broker). The Hanafi school holds that this is not inherently prohibited; rather, it becomes makruh tahrimi when the townspeople are in need of the goods and the broker drives up prices. The proof comes from a hadith and its interpretation by Ibn Abbas. Understanding this helps you see how the school applies the underlying cause (illah) of harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is being prohibited? The act of a townsman selling for a Bedouin. The ruling is makruh tahrimi when townspeople need the goods.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith from Abu Hurairah: 'لا يبيعن حاضر لباد' and the athar from Ibn Abbas explaining it as not becoming a broker.
The dalil is a hadith ahad, so its thubut is zanni.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The prohibition is general, but Ibn Abbas specifies it as acting as a broker, and the harm to locals is the cause (illah).
This allows lifting the prohibition when there is no harm.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school also prohibits, but Hanafi interprets the exception based on need.
The difference stems from whether the hadith is absolute or conditional.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position is that it is only prohibited when there is harm; otherwise permissible.
This is based on the interpretation of Ibn Abbas and the illah of harm.

Source Text

[906] (25) And he prohibited the selling of townspeople to villagers. If the townspeople, for example, have a severe need for grain, yet the merchants are selling grain from the villagers at a higher price, then this is disliked. Because this will harm the townspeople; they are needy and have more right. (2) It is prohibited in the hadith: Abu Hurairah said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited talaqqi and that a townsman sell for a Bedouin (Bukhari, Bab al-Nahy an Talaqqi al-Rukban, p. 289, no. 2162; Muslim, Bab Tahrim Bay' al-Hadhir lil-Badi, p. 4, no. 1520). This hadith prohibits the townsman from selling goods to the villager when there is need. And if the townspeople have no need, it is permissible to sell to the villagers. The evidence for this is the athar: I asked Ibn Abbas, 'What is the meaning of his saying: Let not a townsman sell for a Bedouin?' He said, 'He should not be his broker.' (Bukhari, Bab al-Nahy an Talaqqi al-Rukban, p. 289, no. 12163; Muslim, Bab Hashiyah: (a) He prohibited talaqqi al-jalab and that a townsman sell for a Bedouin (b) He prohibited talaqqi al-jalab and that a townsman sell for a Bedouin (c) Abdullah ibn Abbas was asked about 'let not a townsman sell for a Bedouin' and he said: 'He should not be a broker for him.' Broker is called dallal.)
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage continues the theme of prohibited sales, focusing on bay' al-hadhir lil-badi (townsman selling for Bedouin). The author states the ruling: it is prohibited (makruh) when the townspeople are in need of the goods, because the townsman acting as intermediary drives up prices, harming the needy. The proof is the same hadith as the previous lesson, and additionally the explanation of Ibn Abbas, who interprets 'selling for a Bedouin' as acting as a broker (dallal) to sell at high prices. The author notes that if the townspeople are not in need, the transaction is permissible. This shows that the underlying cause is harm to the local population, not the mere presence of a broker.

Key Terms
بيع الحاضر للبادي (bayʿ al-ḥāḍir lil-bādī): A townsman selling goods on behalf of a villager or acting as a broker, especially when townspeople are in need.
دلال (dallāl): A broker or middleman who facilitates sales, often for a commission.

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of a townsman selling for a Bedouin is not absolute but depends on the need of the townspeople.

Separating Minor Mahram Slaves: Valid Sale, Disliked Act
Ruling on separating two minor slaves who are mahram relatives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on separating minor mahram slaves and explain why the sale remains valid despite being makruh.

Core Idea
Separating minor mahram slaves is makruh but the sale is valid—moral prohibition does not invalidate the contract.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling: a master owns two minor slaves who are mahram relatives (e.g., mother and child). Selling them separately is disliked (makruh) because it causes harm to the minors, yet the sale itself is legally valid. This distinction between contractual validity and moral permissibility is a key feature of Hanafi fiqh. We will explore the evidence from hadith and the reasoning behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is separating two minor mahram slaves by selling or gifting them to different owners. The hukm is makruh tanzihi (disliked but not prohibited).
The text explicitly states 'makruh' and that the sale is 'jayiz' (valid).
2
Apply the condition: minority and mahram
The dislike applies only when at least one slave is a minor and they are mahram (e.g., mother-child, siblings). If both are adults, separation is not disliked.
The basis is the minor's emotional attachment and need for upbringing.
3
Cite the dalil (proof)
The hadith of Abu Ayyub: 'Whoever separates a mother from her child, Allah will separate him from his loved ones on the Day of Judgment.' This warning indicates the act is sinful, hence disliked.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), so the ruling is at the level of makruh, not haram.
4
Distinguish between validity and permissibility
Although the act is disliked, the contract (sale/gift) is valid because the slaves are property. Ownership rights permit the transfer; the prohibition is on the moral harm, not on the contract's essential elements.
This is a classic Hanafi distinction: 'The contract is valid but the action is reproachable.'
5
Note the exception for adults
If both slaves are adults, there is no special harm or attachment, so separation is not disliked. The ruling respects adult autonomy.
This exception helps define the scope of the prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[909] (28) Someone owned two minor slaves, one being a mahram relative of the other, then they should not be separated. Similarly, when one is adult and the other minor. If they are separated, it is disliked. And the sale is valid. And if both are adults, there is no harm in separating them. If both minor slaves, or one minor and one adult, and they are mahram relatives, then separating them by sale or gift is disliked. (1) The minor becomes attached to the other; for example, mother and son, the mother is attached to the son and nurtures him. If separated, both will be distressed and the upbringing will be affected. Therefore, separating them is disliked, yet since they are the property of the master, selling or gifting them is valid. (2) There is harm to the slave in this, so it is disliked. (3) Hadith: From Abu Ayyub, he said: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) say: 'Whoever separates a mother from her child, Allah will separate him from his loved ones on the Day of Judgment.' Another hadith: From Ali, he said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) gave me two brothers as slaves, then I sold one of them. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said to me: O Ali, what did you do?'
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on separating two slaves who are mahram relatives of each other, especially when at least one is a minor. The author states that it is makruh (disliked) to separate them by sale or gift because it causes harm to the minors (like a mother and child). The proof includes a hadith warning and the principle of avoiding harm (la dharar wa la dirar). However, the transaction (sale or gift) itself is valid because the slaves are property of the master. If both are adults, separation is not disliked as there is no special attachment. This ruling applies to all mahram relations, not just mother and child.

Key Terms
ذو رحم محرم (dhū raḥim muḥarrim): A relative by blood who is within the prohibited degrees of marriage, such as mother, sister, daughter, etc.
مملوك (mamlūk): A slave owned by a master; the ruling applies to ownership of human beings, which is now obsolete.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, separating minor mahram slaves is disliked (makruh) but does not invalidate the contract, illustrating the distinction between moral prohibition and legal validity.

Makruh Sales Remain Valid
Ruling that these makruh sales are not fasid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that a makruh sale is valid (sahih) and explain why the contract is not fasid.

Core Idea
A sale that is makruh does not become invalid; the contract's core remains sound.

In this passage, we learn an important distinction: not every prohibited action in a sale renders the contract invalid. The author clarifies that the five previously mentioned makruh sales are valid in essence; only the circumstances make them blameworthy. Understanding this principle is crucial for distinguishing between defects in the contract's core and external prohibitions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State that these sales are makruh but not fasid.
The ruling is clear: the sale is valid.
2
Locate the reason
The defect is not in the substance (sulb al-aqd) but in conditions and other matters.
This distinguishes between core and peripheral issues.
3
Understand the consequence
If the buyer takes possession, ownership transfers validly.
Legal effect despite the prohibition.
4
Note the practical implication
Even though the sale is valid, it should be avoided because it is makruh.
Makruh does not nullify the contract.

۹۰۸) (۲۷) یہ سب مکروہ ہیں لیکن ان سے بیع فاسد نہیں ہوگی۔
او پر پانچ صورتیں بیان کی گئی ہیں جن سے بیع مکر وہ ہوگی لیکن بیچ فاسد نہیں ہوگی ۔
اوپر کی پانچوں صورتوں میں خامی صلب عقد اور اصل عقد میں نہیں ہے بلکہ شرائط اور دیگر چیزوں میں ہے اس لئے بیع فاسد نہیں ہوگی بلکہ صرف مکروہ ہوگی۔ جس کا نتیجہ یہ ہوگا کہ مشتری بیع پر قبضہ کرلے تو مشتری طبیع کا مالک ہو جائے گا البتہ ایسا کرنا مکروہ ہے نہیں کرنا چاہئے ۔ ہر ایک مسئلے کی وجہ اور تشریح گزر چکی ہے۔
908 (27) All these are makruh, but the sale does not become fasid by them. Above, five situations were mentioned which make the sale makruh but the sale does not become fasid. In all five situations, the defect is not in the substance of the contract or the original contract, but in the conditions and other matters. Therefore, the sale does not become fasid, but only makruh. The result is that if the buyer takes possession of the sale item, the buyer becomes the owner of the commodity; however, doing so is makruh and should not be done. The reason and explanation of each issue have already passed.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This ruling clarifies that the five previously mentioned makruh sales (including selling during Friday adhan) are not fasid (invalid). The commentary explains that the defect is not in the essence of the contract but in external conditions or circumstances. Therefore, if the buyer takes possession, ownership transfers validly. This distinction is important: the sale is legally effective but blameworthy. The Hanafi school holds that makruh tanzih does not affect the validity of the transaction.

Key Terms
فاسد (fasid): An invalid contract due to a defect in its core elements (like missing consideration or illegal subject matter).
صلب عقد (sulb al-aqd): The essence of the contract, i.e., the offer, acceptance, and consideration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The buyer does not become owner because the sale is invalid.
B) The buyer becomes the owner but the action is makruh.
C) The sale must be rescinded.
D) The seller can reclaim the item at any time.

Key Takeaway
A sale that is makruh due to external factors remains valid; the contract's core must be defective for it to become fasid.

Ruling on Separating Slaves in Sale
Ruling on separating slaves with hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on separating slave relatives in a sale and apply the correct hukm based on the age of the slaves.

Core Idea
Separating young slave relatives in a sale is makruh, but the sale remains valid; adult slaves may be separated without disapproval.

In the book of sales, the Hanafi school addresses whether it is permissible to separate relatives who are slaves when selling them. This lesson examines the ruling based on age and the evidence from the Sunnah. Understanding this ruling helps apply the principle that ethical considerations can create dislikes without invalidating transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is separating two slaves who are mother-child or siblings by selling them to different buyers. The text states the ruling is makruh (disliked) when one is adult and the other minor, and permissible when both are adults.
Note the distinction based on age: minors need care, adults can fend for themselves.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith from Tirmidhi and the incident with Ali (RA) are cited. The Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded returning the sold brother slave, indicating disapproval of separation.
The hadith is ahad (single narration) but accepted as evidence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'Return him' implies that the sale of one brother alone was disapproved, thus separating young siblings is makruh. The Hanafi school understands this as dislike (karahah) rather than prohibition because the sale is still valid.
The command might be interpreted as nasiha (advice) rather than an order of prohibition.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools, like the Shafi'i, may hold separation of mother and child as haram (prohibited). The Hanafi position distinguishes between young and adult, limiting the dislike to situations where harm may occur.
The difference arises from the interpretation of the hadith and the weight given to potential harm.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that separation of young slave relatives is makruh tanzih and the sale is valid; for adults, it is permissible. This balances the ethical concern with the principle that ownership allows sale, but with dislike when harm is likely.
The later Hanafi masters affirm this position.

الشرح الثميرى الجزء الثانى ٦٠ كتاب البيوع يفرق بينهما وكذلك اذا كان احدهما كبيرا والآخر صغيرا فان فرق بينهما كره ذلك وجاز البيع وان كانا كبيرين فلا بأس بالتفريق بينهما. غلامک فاخبرته فقال رده رده (الف) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی کراہیتہ الفرق بين الاخوین او بین الوالدة وولدها فى البيع ص ۲۴۱ نمبر ۱۳۸۴) اس حدیث میں والدہ اور بھائی کو جدا کرنے سے آپ نے منع فرمایا ہے۔ اس لئے چھوٹے مملوک کے درمیان جدائیگی کرنا مکروہ ہے۔ اور اگر دونوں غلام بڑے ہوں تو جدا کرنے میں کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے۔ حاشیہ : (الف) میں نے حضور سے کہتے سنا، جس نے والدہ اور اس کے بچے کے درمیان تفریق کی اللہ اس کے اور اس کے محبوب کے درمیان قیامت میں تفریق کرے گا۔ حضرت علی فرماتے ہیں کہ مجھے حضور نے دو غلام دیئے جو دونوں بھائی تھے۔ پس میں نے ان میں سے ایک کہ بیچ دیا۔ حضور نے مجھے کہا اے علی ! اپنے غلام کو کیا کیا؟ میں نے ان کو بیچنے کی خبر دی، آپ نے فرمایا اس کر واپس کر لو اس کو واپس کر لو۔
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Part 2, 60. Book of Sales: ... He differentiates between them, and likewise if one is adult and the other minor, and he differentiates between them, that is disapproved (makruh) and the sale is valid. And if both are adults, there is no harm in separating them. ... Your slave, and I informed him, so he said: 'Return him, return him' (Tirmidhi, Chapter on Dislike of Separation Between Brothers or Between Mother and Her Child in Sale). In this hadith, the Prophet forbade separating a mother and a brother. Therefore, separating between young slaves is makruh. And if both slaves are adults, there is no harm in separating them. Footnote (a): I heard the Prophet saying: 'Whoever separates between a mother and her child, Allah will separate between him and his beloved on the Day of Judgment.' Ali narrates: The Prophet gave me two slaves who were brothers. I sold one of them. The Prophet said: 'O Ali, what did you do with your slave?' I informed him of the sale. He said: 'Return him, return him.'
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the book of sales. The author states the general ruling that when a seller wishes to separate a mother from her young child or two siblings in a sale, if one is young and the other adult, separating them is makruh (disliked) but the sale itself is valid. If both are adults, there is no objection to separating them. The hadith from Tirmidhi and the incident with Ali are given as proofs. The Hanafi position: the prohibition is for young slaves because of harm and potential hardship; adult slaves can fend for themselves, so separation is permissible.

Key Terms
الفرق (al-farq): Separating two slaves who are relatives (mother-child or siblings) by selling them to different buyers.
مملوك (mamluk): A slave owned by someone.
كراهة (karahah): Disapproval; a legal classification between permissible and haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) When both slaves are adults
B) When one slave is an adult and the other is a child
C) When both slaves are children
D) When the slaves are not related

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling separates the hukm based on the age of the slaves: separating young slaves from family is makruh tanzih, but the sale is valid; for adults, it is permissible.

Iqalah: Rescission Must Be at the Original Price
Ruling with proof and condition on price

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on iqalah and explain why any stipulation of a different price is void but does not invalidate the rescission.

Core Idea
Iqalah is a rescission, not a new sale — only the original price may be returned.

In Hanafi fiqh, iqalah (mutual rescission of a sale) is a permissible and even meritorious act. However, it is not a new transaction; it is a cancellation of the original contract. Therefore, the parties must return exactly what was originally exchanged — no more, no less. This lesson examines the ruling, its proof from hadith and athar, and the effect of stipulating a different price.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State that iqalah is permissible (ja'iz) for both seller and buyer, but it must be with the return of the original price (mithl al-thaman al-awwal).
The text explicitly says 'iqalah jā'izah ... bi-mithl al-thaman al-awwal'.
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the hadith (from Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah) about forgiveness for one who rescinds, and the athar from Ibn Abbas and Aswad that giving extra is disliked.
The hadith and athar are quoted in the commentary.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The promise of forgiveness indicates permissibility and virtue. The athar show that iqalah is a faskh (rescission), not a new sale, so only the original capital (ra's al-mal) should be returned.
Because it is faskh, any increase or decrease would be a new transaction.
4
Note the condition about stipulation
If the parties stipulate a price more or less than the original, the condition is void (bāṭil), but the iqalah itself remains valid with the original price.
The text says: 'fa al-sharṭu bāṭilun wa yuruddu al-thaman al-awwal'.
5
Understand the basis
The ruling is based on the classification of iqalah as faskh. Since it is a cancellation, the contract is undone exactly as it was; any extra payment would be a new consideration, which is not allowed.
Some other schools treat iqalah as a new sale, but Hanafi insists it is faskh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الاقالة كتاب البيوع [١٠] (١) الاقالة جائزة فى البيع للبائع والمشترى بمثل الثمن الاول [٩١١] (۲) فان شرطوا فيها اكثر من الثمن الاول او اقل فالشرط باطل ويرد الثمن الاول [٩١٠] (۱) اقالہ جائز ہے بیچ میں بائع کے لئے اور مشتری کے لئے ثمن اول کے مثل ہے۔ بائع اور مشتری دونوں کے لئے اقالہ جائز ہے۔ لیکن جس قیمت میں بیچ ہوئی تھی بائع اتنی ہی قیمت واپس کر دیگا، کم بھی نہیں اور زیادہ بھی نہیں۔ بائع نے جتنی قیمت پہلے لی ہے وہی قیمت واپس کرے، اسی کو بمثل الثمن الاول کہا ہے۔ (۱) بائع اور مشتری کے درمیان کوئی نئی بیع نہیں ہے کہ قیمت زیادہ لے یا کم لے بلکہ اقالہ کا مطلب ہے۔ پہلے ہی بیع کو توڑنا ہے اس لئے پہلی ہی قیمت واپس کرے گا (۲) عن ابن عباس انه كره ان يبتاع البيع ثم يرده ويرد معه دراهم وفي هذا دلالة على ان الاقالة فسخ فلا تجوز الابرأس المال (ب) ( سنن سمجھتی ، باب من اقال المسلم اليه بعض المسلم و قبض بعضاج سادس ص ٤٥، نمبر ۱۱۱۳۳) عن الاسود انه كره ان يردها و يرد معها شيئا (ج) مصنف عبد الرزاق ج ثامن ص ۱۹ نمبر (۱۴۱۳) اس اثر میں حضرت عبداللہ بن عباس نے ثمن کے ساتھ مزید کچھ دینے سے کراہیت کا اظہار کیا ہے۔ اقالہ بیع اول کا فسخ ہے۔ [٩١١] (۲) پس اگر پہلی قیمت سے زیادہ کی شرط لگائی یا اس سے کم کی تو شرط باطل ہے، اور ثمن اول ہی لوٹایا جائے گا۔ مثلا چارسو میں مبیع خریدی تھی اور مشتری نے اقالہ کے لئے پانچ سو درہم مانگے یا بائع نے کہا کہ اقالہ کے لئے تین سو دوں گا تو یہ کی زیادتی کی شرط باطل ہے۔ البتہ اس میں شرط لگانے سے اقالہ باطل نہیں ہوگا بلکہ ثمن اول ہی پر اقالہ ہوگا۔ اوپر ابن عباس کا اثر گزر چکا ہے کہ زیادہ دینا وہ مکروہ سمجھتے تھے۔ حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا کسی نے مسلمان سے اقالہ کیا تو اللہ اس کے گناہوں کو معاف کر دے گا (ب) حضرت عبد اللہ بن عباس نا پسند کرتے تھے کہ آدمی بیچ کرے پھر اس کو واپس لوٹائے اور اس کے ساتھ کچھ درہم لوٹائے۔ اس قول میں اس بات پر دلالت ہے کہ اقالہ کرنا بیچ کو فسخ کرتا ہے۔ اس لئے نہیں جائز ہے مگر راس المال یعنی پہلی قیمت کے ساتھ (ج) حضرت اسود نا پسند فرماتے تھے کہ مبیع واپس کرے اور اس کے ساتھ کچھ اور بھی واپس کرے۔
Chapter of Iqalah. Book of Sales. [10] (1) Iqalah is permissible in sale for the seller and the buyer with a return of the first price. [911] (2) If they stipulate in it more than the first price or less, the condition is void and the first price is returned. [910] (1) Iqalah is permissible in sale for the seller and the buyer; it is with the like of the first price. It is permissible for both seller and buyer. But the price at which the sale occurred, the seller will return exactly that price, neither less nor more. The price the seller previously took, he returns the same; this is called 'like the first price'. (1) There is no new sale between seller and buyer by which the price could be increased or decreased; rather the meaning of iqalah is to annul the first sale, so he returns the first price. (2) From Ibn Abbas that he disliked that one makes a sale, then returns it and returns with it dirhams. In this there is evidence that iqalah is a rescission, so it is not permissible except with the capital. (b) (Sunan ...) From Aswad that he disliked that one returns it and returns with it something. (c) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq) In this athar, Abdullah ibn Abbas expressed dislike for giving something extra with the price. Iqalah is the rescission of the first sale. [911] (2) So if they stipulate in it more than the first price or less, the condition is void, and the first price is returned. For example, the item was bought for four hundred, and the buyer demands five hundred dirhams for iqalah, or the seller says I will give three hundred for iqalah, such condition of excess is void. However, the iqalah does not become void due to the condition; rather iqalah will be based on the first price. The athar of Ibn Abbas above passed that giving extra he considered disliked. Footnote (a): The Prophet said: 'Whoever rescinds a sale with a Muslim, Allah will forgive his sins.' (b) Abdullah ibn Abbas disliked that a person makes a sale, then returns it and returns with it some dirhams. This statement indicates that iqalah rescinds the sale, so it is not permissible except with the capital (i.e., the first price). (c) Aswad disliked that one returns the item and returns with it something else.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on iqalah (rescission) in the book of sales. The author first states that iqalah is permissible for both parties, but it must be with the return of the original price exactly. If they stipulate a different price, the condition is void, but the iqalah itself remains valid with the original price. The evidence includes a hadith promising forgiveness for one who rescinds, and athar from Ibn Abbas and Aswad showing that giving extra is disliked because iqalah is a faskh (rescission) of the original contract, not a new sale. The Hanafi position emphasizes that iqalah is a cancellation, not a new transaction, so only the original price should be exchanged.

Key Terms
الاقالة (al-iqalah): The mutual rescission of a sale by both parties, returning the goods and the price.
الفسخ (al-faskh): Legal annulment or rescission of a contract, restoring parties to pre-contract status.
الثمن الأول (al-thaman al-awwal): The original price paid in the first sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Iqalah is a mutual rescission that must return exactly the original price; any stipulation for a different price is void, but the rescission itself remains valid.

Permissibility and Price Condition in Iqaalah
Ruling on permissibility and price condition with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on iqaalah and identify the condition that it must be at the original price, citing the hadith and athar proofs.

Core Idea
Iqaalah is permissible at the original price; any stipulation of more or less is void.

In this lesson, we explore the fundamental ruling of iqaalah — the mutual rescission of a sale. The passage establishes that iqaalah is not only permissible but encouraged, provided it is done at the exact original price. Any attempt to increase or decrease the price invalidates the condition but not the rescission itself. We will examine the hadith and the practice of the Companions that underpin this rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is iqaalah? The passage defines it as mutual rescission when the seller or buyer regrets. The hukm is ja'iz (permissible) and even afdal (preferable).
The act is rescission of a sale, not a new sale.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith from Abu Huraira: 'Whoever rescinds for a Muslim, Allah will rescind his sins.' Identify its source (Sunan Abu Dawood, Ibn Majah).
This is a hadith ahad.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove permissibility? The promise of forgiveness indicates recommendation (nadb), not obligation.
The verb 'aqala' is an action, and the reward implies desirability.
4
Examine the price condition
The passage states that iqaalah must be at the first price. Support from Ibn Abbas's athar disliking extra payment.
The athar indicates iqaalah is faskh (rescission), so no extra can be taken.
5
Apply the condition
If a different price is stipulated, the condition is void but iqaalah is still valid at the original price.
Example: bought for 400, asking 500: condition void, but iqaalah valid at 400.

كتاب البيوع
[١٠] (١) الاقالة جائزة فى البيع للبائع والمشترى بمثل الثمن الاول [٩١١] (۲) فان
باب الاقالة )
رداری نے اقالہ کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ بائع مبیع بیچنے کے بعد نادم ہو جائے کہ میں نے غلط بیچ دیا، پھر مشتری سے کہے کہ مجھے مبیع واپس کر دیں اور ثمن واپس لے لیں اور مشتری ایسا کر دے تو اس کو اقالہ کہتے ہیں۔ یا مشتری خریدنے پر نادم ہو جائے اور بائع سے کہے کہ مبیع واپس لے لیں اور ثمن دے دیں اور بائع ایسا کرے تو اس کو اقالہ کہتے ہیں۔ ایسا کرنا جائز ہے بلکہ افضل ہے۔ حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے عن ابی ھریرة قال قال رسول الله من اقال مسلما اقاله الله عشرته (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی فضل الا قالت ج ثانی ص ۱۳۴ نمبر ۳۴۶۰ ابن ماجہ شریف، باب الا قالۃ ص ۳۱۵ نمبر ۲۱۹۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ اقالہ کرنا جائز ہے بلکہ سامنے والے کی مجبوری ہو تو ا قالہ یعنی مبیع واپس کرنے میں ثواب ملے گا۔
[۹۱۰) (۱) اقالہ جائز ہے بیچ میں بائع کے لئے اور مشتری کے لئے شمن اول کے مثل ہے۔ بائع اور مشتری دونوں کے لئے اقالہ جائز ہے۔ لیکن جس قیمت میں بیچ ہوئی تھی بائع اتنی ہی قیمت واپس کر دیگا، کم بھی نہیں اور زیادہ بھی نہیں۔ بائع نے جتنی قیمت پہلے لی ہے وہی قیمت واپس کرے، اسی کو بمثل الثمن الاول کہا ہے۔ (۱) بائع اور مشتری کے درمیان کوئی نئی بیع نہیں ہے کہ قیمت زیادہ لے یا کم لے بلکہ اقالہ کا مطلب ہے۔ پہلے ہی بیع کو توڑنا ہے اس لئے پہلی ہی قیمت واپس کرے گا (۲) عن ابن عباس انه كره ان يبتاع البيع ثم يرده ويرد معه دراهم وفي هذا دلالة على ان الاقالة فسخ فلا تجوز الابرأس المال (ب) ( سنن سمجھتی ، باب من اقال المسلم اليه بعض المسلم و قبض بعضاج سادس ص ۴۵، نمبر ۱۱۱۳۳) عن الاسود انه كره ان يردها و يرد معها شيئا (ج) مصنف عبد الرزاق ج ثامن ص ۱۹ نمبر (۱۴۱۳) اس اثر میں حضرت عبداللہ بن عباس نے شمن کے ساتھ مزید کچھ دینے سے کراہیت کا اظہار کیا ہے۔
اقالہ بیع اول کا فسخ ہے۔
،
[۹۱۱] (۲) پس اگر پہلی قیمت سے زیادہ کی شرط لگائی یا اس سے کم کی تو شرط باطل ہے، اور ثمن اول ہی لوٹایا جائے گا۔ مثلا چارسو میں مبیع خریدی تھی اور مشتری نے اقالہ کے لئے پانچ سو درہم مانگے یا بائع نے کہا کہ اقالہ کے لئے تین سو دوں گا تو یہ کی زیادتی کی شرط باطل ہے۔ البتہ اس میں شرط لگانے سے اقالہ باطل نہیں ہوگا بلکہ ثمن اول ہی پرا قالہ ہوگا۔
او پر ابن عباس کا اثر گزر چکا ہے کہ زیادہ دینا وہ مکروہ سمجھتے تھے۔
حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا کسی نے مسلمان سے اقالہ کیا تو اللہ اس کے گناہوں کو معاف کر دے گا (ب) حضرت عبد اللہ بن عباس نا پسند کرتے تھے کہ آدمی بیچ کرے پھر اس کو واپس لوٹائے اور اس کے ساتھ کچھ درہم لوٹائے۔ اس قول میں اس بات پر دلالت ہے کہ اقالہ کرنا بیچ کو فتح کرتا ہے۔ اس لئے نہیں جائز ہے مگر راس المال یعنی پہلی قیمت کے ساتھ (ج) حضرت اسود نا پسند فرماتے تھے کہ مبیع واپس کرے اور اس کے ساتھ کچھ اور بھی واپس کرے۔

شرط اکثر منه فالشرط باطل ويرد بمثل الثمن الاول [۱۲] (۳) وهي فسخ في حق المتعاقدين بيع جديد في حق غيرهما في قول ابي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى [۹۱۳] (۴) وهلاك الثمن لا يمنع صحة الاقالة وهلاك المبيع يمنع صحتها ( ۱۹۱۴ (۵) وان شمن پر اس وقت اقالہ ہوگا جبکہ مبیع میں کوئی عیب نہ ہوا ہو۔ اگر مبیع میں عیب ہو گیا تو مشتری کم قیمت واپس کر سکتا ہے۔

(۱۹۱۳ (۴) اور شمن کا ہلاک ہونا اقالہ کے صحیح ہونے کو نہیں روکتا اور مبیع کا ہلاک ہونا اس کے صحیح ہونے کو روکتا ہے۔ شمن ہلاک ہو جائے ، بائع کے پاس نہ رہے تب بھی اقالہ ہو سکتا ہے۔ لیکن مشتری کے پاس مبیع ہلاک ہو جائے تو اقالہ نہیں ہو سکے گا۔ (۱) اصل واپسی مبیع کی ہے ۔ وہی متعین کرنے سے متعین ہوتی ہے۔ قیمت اور روپیہ تو کوئی سا بھی دے گا۔ اس لئے اگر مبیع ہلاک ہو جائے تو کس چیز کو واپس کرے گا؟ اس لئے مبیع ہلاک ہونے کے بعد اقالہ نہیں ہو سکے گا۔ اور ثشمن ہلاک ہو جائے تو یہ پونڈ نہیں دوسرے پونڈ بائع واپس کر دے گا۔ اس لئے شمن کے ہلاک ہونے کے باوجودا قالہ ہوسکتا ہے۔
اصول اقالہ میں اصل واپسی مبیع کی ہوتی ہے۔ (۱۹۱۴ (۵) اگر بعض مبیع ہلاک ہو جائے تو باقی میں اقالہ جائز ہے۔
