Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Fraud in Murabahah and Tawliyah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on deducting fraud in murabahah and tawliyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on fraud in murabahah and tawliyah, and explain the practical difference between deduction and option.

Core Idea
When fraud occurs in a cost-plus or profit sale, Hanafi imams differ: deduct the fraud, or uphold the price but grant an option to cancel.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute concerning fraud in two types of sale where the seller misstates the cost. The question is whether the buyer should be entitled to a price reduction or merely the option to rescind. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to apply khiyar al-tadlis and to appreciate the subtleties of the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fraud scenario
The seller lies about the cost in both murabahah (cost + profit) and tawliyah (cost only). Determine the fraudulent amount.
Example: bought for 10, lied that cost was 13, then sold at murabahah for 15 (13+2 profit) or tawliyah for 13.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position (from earlier passage)
According to the previous discussion, Abu Hanifa holds that in tawliyah, the fraudulent amount is deducted. His position on murabahah is not explicitly given here, but the toolbox indicates he only ruled on tawliyah.
The earlier passage (7) is not provided, but we rely on the given toolbox.
3
State Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf: deduct the fraudulent amount in both murabahah and tawliyah. The buyer pays the adjusted price.
In the example, murabahah price becomes 12 (15-3), tawliyah price becomes 10 (13-3).
4
State Muhammad's position
Muhammad: no deduction in either contract. The agreed price stands. However, the buyer is given the option (khiyar) to cancel the sale due to the fraud.
The sale is valid at the agreed price, but the buyer can rescind if they wish.
5
Compare practical outcomes
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf reduce the price; Muhammad maintains the price but gives an option. The key difference is whether the buyer automatically gets a lower price or must choose to cancel.
The thamarah al-khilaf is whether the sale is automatically adjusted or the buyer must act.

[ ۹۲۲] (۸) وقال ابو يوسف رحمه الله تعالى يحط فيهما وقال محمد رحمه الله تعالى لا يحط فيهما لكن يخير فيهما اور امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا دونوں صورتوں میں کم کیا جائے گا، اور امام محمد نے فرمایا دونوں صورتوں میں کم نہیں کیا جائے گا لیکن اور ابو نے [؟] اور امام نے فرمایا دونوں کیا جائے لیکن دونوں کو اختیار دیا جائے گا۔ امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ تولیہ اور مرابحہ دونوں صورتوں میں جتنی قیمت جھوٹ بول کر لی ہے اتنی قیمت کم کر کے مشتری کو لینے کا اختیار ہوگا۔ مثلا مثال مذکور میں دس پونڈ میں خریدا تھا اور جھوٹ بولا تھا کہ تیرہ پونڈ میں خریدا ہے تو تین پونڈ جھوٹ بول کر لئے تھے اس لئے مرابحہ اور تولیہ دونوں صورتوں میں تین پونڈ کم کر کے لے گا۔ اس لئے مرابحہ کی شکل میں پندرہ کی بجائے بارہ پونڈ دے گا اور تولیہ کی شکل میں دس پونڈ ہی دے گا۔ امام محمد قرماتے ہیں کہ مرابحہ اور تولیہ دونوں صورتوں میں کم نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ بائع نے ترغیب دینے کے لئے مرابحہ اور تولیہ کی بات کی ہے۔ اصل مقصود تو وہ قیمت ہے جس پر بات طے ہوئی ہے۔ بائع مرابحہ میں مثلا پندرہ پونڈ اور تولیہ میں مثلا تیرہ پونڈ سے کم پر دینے کے لئے راضی نہیں ہے۔ اور اس پر بات بھی طے ہوئی ہے اس لئے اس سے کم نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ البتہ چونکہ بائع جھوٹ بولا ہے اس لئے مشتری کو لینے نہ لینے کا اختیار ہوگا۔ انکا اصول یہ ہے کہ جس قیمت پر بات طے ہوئی ہے وہی لازم ہوگی۔ مرابحہ اور تولیہ کا لفظ تر غیب کے لئے ہے۔ انت محط : کم کیا جائے گا مشتق ہے حط سے کم کرنا۔
And Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, said: He deducts in both. And Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, said: He does not deduct in both, but gives him the choice in both. And Imam Abu Yusuf said: In both tawliyah and murabahah, the amount taken by lying will be deducted, and the buyer will have the option to take it at that reduced price. For example, in the mentioned example, he bought for ten pounds and lied that he bought for thirteen, so he took three pounds by lying. Therefore, in both murabahah and tawliyah, he will deduct three pounds and take it. In murabahah, he will pay twelve instead of fifteen, and in tawliyah, he will pay ten. Imam Muhammad said: In both murabahah and tawliyah, no deduction will be made. The seller mentioned murabahah or tawliyah to give incentive. The real intention is the price agreed upon. The seller is not willing to give it for less than, say, fifteen in murabahah or thirteen in tawliyah. And the contract was made on that, so no deduction. However, since the seller lied, the buyer has the option to take or leave. Their principle is that the agreed price is binding. The words murabahah and tawliyah are for incentive. 'Mahat' means deduction, derived from 'hatt' (to reduce).
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf concerning fraud in both murabahah (profit sale) and tawliyah (cost sale). Imam Abu Yusuf holds that in both types, the fraudulent excess is deducted from the price. For example, if the seller claimed a cost of 13 when actual cost was 10, in tawliyah the buyer pays 10, and in murabahah (if profit was added on the false cost, e.g., 15), the buyer pays 12 (i.e., the false price minus the fraud). Imam Muhammad holds that no deduction is made in either contract; the agreed price stands because the seller used murabahah or tawliyah as a sales technique, not as a guarantee of exact cost. However, since the seller lied, the buyer is given the option (khiyar) to rescind the contract or affirm it. The principle is that the agreed price is binding. The text notes that the word 'mahat' (deduction) is derived from 'hatt' (to lower). This dispute shows the nuanced Hanafi approach to fraud in sale contracts.

Key Terms
المرابحة (al-murabahah): A sale where the seller discloses the cost and adds a stated profit.
التخيير (al-takhyir): Giving the buyer the option to cancel or confirm the sale due to fraud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding fraud in murabahah and tawliyah?
A) Abu Yusuf deducts in both; Muhammad deducts in neither.
B) Abu Yusuf deducts only in tawliyah; Muhammad deducts in both.
C) Abu Yusuf gives option; Muhammad deducts.
D) Both agree on deduction in murabahah only.

Key Takeaway
There is no single Hanafi remedy for fraud in murabahah/tawliyah: the ikhtilaf among the founders gives the mufti a choice between deduction and option depending on context.

Prohibition of Selling Movable Goods Before Possession
Ruling with proof: prohibition of resale before possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reselling movable items before possession and identify the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Selling movable goods before possession is invalid—risk of loss makes it akin to selling what you do not own.

Imagine you buy a crate of dates but haven't taken it home yet. Can you immediately resell it to your neighbor? This passage addresses that very scenario: the Prophet forbade selling food before taking delivery, and the Hanafi school extends this to all movable goods. By the end, you'll understand the ruling, its evidence, and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the buyer reselling a movable good before taking possession. The ruling is that it is not permissible (ja'iz nahi) — the sale is invalid.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The passage cites two hadith: 'Whoever buys food, let him not sell it until he takes full delivery' and 'Do not sell what is not with you.' Identify the source and wording.
Both hadith are found in Bukhari, Muslim, and Abu Dawud.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof proves the ruling)
The prohibition is expressed as 'لا يبعه' which is a clear nahy (prohibition) indicating tahrim (impermissibility or invalidity). The phrase 'حتى يقبضه' makes possession a condition for resale.
In Hanafi usul, a prohibition in a transactional matter renders the contract invalid (batil).
4
Understand the extension via qiyas
The hadith specifically mentions food, but the Hanafi school extends it to all movable goods (manqulat) because the effective cause (illa) is the risk of loss before possession, which applies to all movables.
This qiyas is of the type jaliyy: the illa is clearly present in both cases.
5
Apply the rule
Given a scenario (e.g., buying a phone but not yet receiving it), conclude that reselling it before possession is invalid. The contract would be void.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۹۲۳] (۹) ومن اشترى شيئا مما ينقل ويحول لم يجز له بيعه حتى يقبضه كسی نے کوئی ایسی چیز خریدی جو منتقل ہو سکتی ہے تو اس کی بیع جائز نہیں ہے جب تک اس پر قبضہ نہ کر لے۔ منتقل ہونے والی چیز پر قبضہ کرے تب اس کو آگے بیچے۔ کیونکہ قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے بیچے گا تو ہوسکتا ہے کہ وہ چیز ضائع ہو جائے اور اس کے پاس نہ آئے تو کیسے بیچے گا (۲) پہلے حدیث گزر چکی ہے جو چیز تمہارے پاس نہ ہو اس کو نہ بیچو، لاتبع ماليس عندک (ابوداؤد شریف نمبر ۳۵۰۳) (۳) حدیث میں ہے کہ مبیع پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے مت بیچو عن ابن عمر ان النبی الله قال من ابتاع طعاما فلا يبيعه حتى ليستوفيه زاد اسمعيل فلا يبعه حتى يقبضه (الف) ( بخاری شریف، بیع الطعام قبل ان يقبض و بیع مالیس عندک ص ۲۸۶ نمبر ۲۱۳۶ مسلم شریف، باب بطلان بی اسمیع قبل القبض ص ۵ نمبر ۱۵۲۵ ابوداود شریف ،نمبر۳۳۹۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مطبع پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے اس کو مت بیچو، اس لئے منقولی چیز پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے بیچنا جائز نہیں۔
And whoever buys something that can be moved and transferred, it is not permissible for him to sell it until he takes possession of it. He does not sell it until he takes possession of the movable thing. Because if he sells it before possession, it may be that the item is lost and does not come to him; then how will he sell it? (2) The hadith has already passed: 'Do not sell what is not with you, la tabe' ma laysa 'indak.' (Abu Dawud, no. 3503) (3) In the hadith: 'Do not sell the sold item before possession.' From Ibn Umar that the Prophet said: 'Whoever buys food, let him not sell it until he takes full delivery.' Isma'il added: 'Let him not sell it until he takes possession.' (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud) This hadith shows that selling before possession is not permissible.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with its proof: it is not permissible for the buyer of a movable item to resell it until he takes physical possession (qabd). The reason is that before possession, the item may perish, and selling something not in one's custody falls under the prohibition of selling what one does not possess. The proof is the hadith: 'Do not sell what is not with you' (la tabe' ma laysa 'indak) and the specific hadith of Ibn Umar regarding food: 'Whoever buys food, let him not sell it until he takes full delivery.' This hadith, though specific to food, is extended by analogy to all movable goods. The Hanafi school applies this prohibition to all manqulat (movable items) because of the risk of destruction. The passage also includes the footnote with full hadith references.

Key Terms
المنقول (al-manqul): Movable items that can be physically transferred and are subject to risk of loss.
القبض (al-qabd): Taking physical possession or delivery of the purchased item.
العلة (al-illah): The effective cause or reason behind a legal ruling, used in qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Immediately after the contract.
B) Only after taking possession.
C) Only after paying the full price.
D) Anytime before possession.

Key Takeaway
Selling a movable good before taking possession is invalid (batil) because of the risk of loss, supported by prophetic hadith and qiyas.

Selling Land Before Possession: The Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on selling immovable property before possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on selling 'aqar before possession and explain the basis for the disagreement between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
Land before possession is permissible because the prohibition applies only to food and movables, not immovables.

The classical Hanafi school has a clear difference on whether you can sell real estate (al-'aqar) before actually taking delivery. This lesson walks through the positions of the three founding imams—Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani—and the evidence each uses. By the end, you'll understand why the majority Hanafi view allows this transaction and how a key specification of the general hadith shapes the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is selling immovable property (land, buildings) before the buyer takes physical possession. The dispute: is it permissible or not?
Immovable = al-'aqar; movable = al-manqul.
2
State the majority Hanafi view
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that it is permissible (mubah). Their reasoning: land is not movable and does not carry the risk of destruction that justifies the prohibition.
This is the mufta bihi (operative) position.
3
State the opposing view within the school
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani holds it is not permissible (haram). He relies on the general hadith forbidding the sale of any item before possession.
Imam Muhammad was a direct student of Abu Hanifa.
4
Examine the evidence of the majority
They cite two athar: (1) Ibn Abbas said the Prophet's prohibition was specifically 'food, until it is taken possession of'; (2) Ibn Sirin said there is no harm in buying something that is not measured or weighed (i.e., not food) and selling it before possession.
These athar specify the general hadith, limiting its scope to movables.
5
Understand Imam Muhammad's position and the tarjih
Imam Muhammad takes the hadith 'Do not sell what you do not possess' as absolute. However, the majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) argue that the athar of Ibn Abbas is a legitimate specification (takhsis). The later school (mufta bihi) follows the majority view.
The tarjih is based on the strength of the specification and the absence of risk in land.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۴](١٠) ويجوز بيع العقار قبل القبض عند ابي حنيفة وابي يوسف رحمهما الله وقال محمد رحمه الله تعالى لا يجوز اور جائز ہے زمین کو بیچنا قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اور امام محمد نے فرمایا جائز نہیں۔ زمین منقولی چیز نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے اس میں ہلاکت کا خطرہ نہیں ہے اس لئے اس کو قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے بیچ دیا تو جائز ہے (۲) حضرت عبداللہ بن عباس نے فرمایا کہ قبضہ کرنے کی شرط غلہ وغیرہ میں ہے۔ جس سے اندازہ ہوا کہ زمین وغیرہ پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے بیچنا جائز ہے سمعت ابن عباس يقول اما الذي نهى عنه النبي فهو الطعام ان يباع حتى يقبض (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب بیع الطعام قبل ان يقبض و بیچ مالیس عندك ص ۲۸۶ نمبر ۲۱۳۵) اس اثر میں ہے کہ غلے کے بارے میں ہے قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے نہ بیچے۔ اس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ زمین وغیرہ کو قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے بیچ سکتا ہے (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابن سیرین قـال لا بأس ان يشترى شيئا لا يكال ولا يوزن بنقد ثم يبيعه قبل ان يقبضه (ج) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الرجل یشتری الشی، مالا ریکال ولا یوزن حل پیعہ قبل ان يقبضه ، ج ٹامن، ص ۴۳، نمبر ۱۴۲۳۰) امام محمد فرماتے ہیں کہ زمین کو بھی قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ ان کی دلیل پہلی والی حدیث ہے جس میں مطلقا قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
And it is permissible to sell real estate before possession according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on them. And Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, said: It is not permissible. It is permissible to sell land before taking possession according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad said it is not permissible. Land is not a movable item, so there is no risk of destruction. Therefore, selling it before possession is permissible. (2) Abdullah ibn Abbas said: The condition of possession is only for grains and the like. From this it is understood that selling land before possession is permissible. He said: I heard Ibn Abbas say: 'What the Prophet prohibited is food, that it be sold until it is taken possession.' (Bukhari) This athar shows it is about grains; that it should not be sold before possession. Its meaning is that land and the like can be sold before possession. (2) Also an athar: Ibn Sirin said: 'There is no harm in buying something that is not measured or weighed by cash and then selling it before taking possession.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq) Imam Muhammad says that selling land before possession is also not permissible. His proof is the first hadith which absolutely forbids selling before possession.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sale of immovable property (aqar) before taking possession. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that it is permissible because land is not movable and thus not subject to the risk of destruction that justifies the prohibition. They support this with the athar of Ibn Abbas, who specified that the prohibition of selling before possession applies only to food (and by analogy to movable goods). Similarly, the athar of Ibn Sirin indicates that items which are not measured or weighed (i.e., non-movable) can be sold before possession. On the other hand, Imam Muhammad holds that the general prohibition covers all items, including real estate, because the hadith 'Do not sell what is not with you' is absolute. This dispute illustrates how the Hanafi imams differ on the scope of the hadith prohibition.

Key Terms
العقار (al-aqar): Immovable property such as land and buildings.
الاثر (al-athar): Here means a narration from a Companion (Ibn Abbas) or a Tabi'i (Ibn Sirin), cited as evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following correctly identifies the mufta bihi position regarding the sale of land before possession in the Hanafi school?
A) It is prohibited, following Imam Muhammad.
B) It is permissible, following Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
C) It is permissible only if the buyer takes possession within a week.
D) It is prohibited unless the contract is notarized.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits selling immovable property before possession because the prohibition is specified to food and movables, and the risk of destruction does not apply to land.

Requirement of Remeasuring or Reweighing for Resale
Ruling that measured or weighed items must be remeasured when resold

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on resale of measured or weighed items and identify the condition that triggers the requirement of remeasurement.

Core Idea
A sale by measure or weight requires a fresh measurement for the new buyer — the first measurement does not carry over.

When you buy wheat by measure, you measure it and take possession. Later, if you wish to sell that same wheat by measure to someone else, can you simply use the original measurement? According to the Hanafi school, you cannot. The ruling you are about to read establishes a crucial principle: every sale by measure or weight demands its own measurement or weighing, witnessed by the new buyer. This ensures transparency and eliminates ambiguity in the transaction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its hukm
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is selling a measured or weighed item by the same method (measure or weight) without remeasuring. The hukm is that this is not permissible (haram) until remeasuring is done.
The ruling applies to both the seller and the buyer; the buyer is also prohibited from consuming the item until remeasured.
2
Understand the scope
Which items are covered? Only items that were originally purchased by measure (e.g., wheat, rice) or by weight (e.g., dirhams, dananir), and are now being resold by the same standard. If resold by lump sum or estimation, the ruling does not apply.
The item must have been delivered after measurement into the buyer's possession.
3
Contrast with other modes of sale
If the resale is by estimate (jizaf) or by unit count, remeasuring is not required because the new buyer does not rely on a prior measurement.
This distinction is essential to avoid applying the rule too broadly.
4
Note the rationale
The requirement protects the new buyer from uncertainty (gharar). Each transaction must have its own independent determination of quantity, witnessed by the parties.
The commentary mentions the new buyer's right to witness the measurement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۹۲۵] (۱۱) ومن اشترى مكيلا مكايلة او موزونا موازنة فاكتاله او اتزنه ثم باعه مكايلة او موازنة لم يجز للمشترى منه ان يبيعه ولا ان يأكله حتى يعيد الكيل والوزن. کیلی چیز مثلا گیہوں چاول اور وزنی چیز مثلا درہم اور دنا نیر کیل اور وزن سے خریدا۔ اور کیل یا وزن کر کے بائع سے لیا۔ اب اس کو دو بارہ کیل کر کے یا وزن کر کے بیچنا چاہتا ہے انکل سے نہیں تو پہلا کیل کیا ہو یا وزن کیا ہوا کافی نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ اگلے مشتری کے سامنے دوبارہ کیل کرنا ہوگا۔ یا وزنی چیز ہے تو وزن کرنا ہوگا۔ حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا جس نے غلہ بیچا تو اس کو نہ بیچے یہاں تک کہ اس کو پورا لے لے ، راوی اسمعیل نے یہ بھی فرمایا کہ اس کو نہ بیچے جب تک کہ اس پر قبضہ نہ کرنے (ب) بہر حال جس سے حضور نے روکا ہے وہ غلہ جات ہیں کہ قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے بیچا جائے (ج) حضرت ابن سیرین نے فرمایا کوئی حرج نہیں ہے کہ آدمی کوئی ایسی چیز خریدے جو نہ کیل کی جاتی ہو اور نہ وزن کی جاتی ہو نقد کے ذریعہ پھر اس کو قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے بیچے۔
And whoever buys something measured by measure or weighed by weight, and he measures it or weighs it, then sells it by measure or weight, it is not permissible for the buyer from him to sell it nor to eat it until he repeats the measure or weight. For example, a measured item like wheat or rice, and a weighed item like dirhams or dananir, bought by measure or weight. He measured or weighed and took it from the seller. Now he wants to sell it again by measure or weight, but the first measurement or weighing is not sufficient. Rather, he must re-measure it in front of the next buyer, or if it is weighed, he must weigh it again. Footnote: (a) The Prophet said: Whoever sells grain, let him not sell it until he takes full delivery. (b) In any case, what the Prophet forbade is grains that are sold before possession. (c) Ibn Sirin said: There is no harm in a person buying something that is not measured or weighed by cash and then selling it before possession.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling regarding items sold by measure (like wheat) or by weight (like silver). If a person buys such items, measures or weighs them upon receipt, and then wishes to resell them by the same method (measure or weight), he must re-measure or re-weigh them in the presence of the new buyer. The initial measurement is not sufficient because the new buyer has the right to witness the measurement. This is to ensure transparency and avoid ambiguity. The ruling applies only when reselling by the same standard; if selling by estimate or lump sum, remeasuring may not be required. The footnotes relate previous hadith about the prohibition of selling before possession, but here the emphasis is on the necessity of fresh measurement for the second sale. This rule ensures that each transaction has its own clear determination of quantity.

Key Terms
المكايلة (al-mukayalah): Sale by volume measurement using a standard measure.
الموازنة (al-muwazanah): Sale by weight using a scale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Use the same measurement from when he bought it.
B) Re-measure it in front of the new buyer.
C) Convert to weight instead.
D) No measurement is needed.

Key Takeaway
For a valid resale by measure or weight, the seller must remeasure or reweigh the item for each new buyer.

Selling Real Estate Before Possession: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on selling land before qabd with proofs from hadith and Companions' practices.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on selling real estate before qabd, explain the evidence for each view, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Land is not movable; the prohibition on selling before qabd applies only to perishables, not real estate.

The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on whether real estate can be sold before taking physical possession. This lesson unpacks the dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, who permit it, and Imam Muhammad, who prohibits it. We will examine the textual evidence and the underlying reasoning to understand why the majority view prevails.

Guided Path
1
Identify the positions
State the three imams' views: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf permit; Muhammad forbids. Note that the majority view is permissibility.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
2
Examine the primary proof
The hadith of Ibn Umar: 'Whoever buys food should not sell it until he takes possession.' The Hanafi majority focus on the word 'food' to restrict the ruling.
The hadith is in Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Understand the illa
The rationale behind the prohibition is the risk of destruction or loss (gharar). Land is not perishable, so the illa is absent.
Imam Muhammad argues the hadith is general and includes all items.
4
Consider Companions' practice
Ibn Abbas limited the prohibition to food; Ibn Sirin allowed selling non-measured/non-weighed items before qabd. This supports the majority view.
These athar are cited in the source.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is relied upon in the Hanafi school. The permissibility of selling real estate before qabd is the operative ruling.
Imam Muhammad's view is marjuh.

Source Text

ان کی دلیل پہلی والی حدیث ہے جس میں مطلقا قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
It is permissible to sell real estate before taking possession according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on them, and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, said it is not permissible. Number 3503) (3) In the hadith: 'Do not sell the sold item before taking possession.' From Ibn Umar that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever buys food should not sell it until he takes full possession.' Isma'il added: 'He should not sell it until he receives it.' (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud). This hadith indicates that one should not sell before taking possession; therefore, selling movable property before taking possession is not permissible. Justification: [924] (10) And it is permissible to sell land before taking possession according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad said it is not permissible. Land is not movable property, so there is no risk of destruction; therefore, it is permissible to sell it before taking possession. (2) Abdullah ibn Abbas said: 'The condition of taking possession applies to grain and the like.' This indicates that it is permissible to sell land and the like before taking possession. I heard Ibn Abbas say: 'What the Prophet forbade is food, that it should be sold until it is taken possession.' (Bukhari). This tradition is about grain, not to sell before taking possession. This implies that land etc. can be sold before taking possession. (2) Another tradition: Ibn Sirin said: 'There is no harm in a person buying something that is not measured or weighed for cash and then selling it before taking possession.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq). Imam Muhammad says that selling land before taking possession is also not permissible. His evidence is the first hadith which absolutely forbids selling before taking possession.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sale of real estate (like land) before taking physical possession (qabd). The majority of the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) permit it, while Imam Muhammad prohibits it. The key distinction is that land is immovable ('aqar) and not subject to the same risk of destruction or loss as movable goods. Therefore, the general prohibition on selling before qabd, which is based on hadith concerning food/grain, does not apply to land. The author supports the permissibility view with the reasoning that the hadith specifically mentions 'food', and the Companion Ibn Abbas restricted the ruling to food. Furthermore, Ibn Sirin's tradition indicates that items not measured or weighed (i.e., items that are not perishable) may be sold before qabd. Imam Muhammad, however, holds the general hadith as absolute and includes all types of property. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is the permissibility of selling real estate before qabd, as this is the view of the two senior imams and is supported by the evidence of the Companions.

Key Terms
عقار ('aqar): Land or real estate; immovable property.
قبض (qabd): Taking physical possession of the purchased item.
منقول (manqul): Movable property that can be transported.

Key Takeaway

Re-Measuring and Re-Weighing Before Resale
Ruling that a buyer must re-measure/re-weigh before selling by measure/weight

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a buyer must re-measure/re-weigh goods before reselling them by measure/weight, and identify the proofs (Quran 83:3, hadith from Bukhari and Ibn Majah) that support this ruling.

Core Idea
The buyer must re-measure/re-weigh before reselling by measure/weight — the first measurement is for the seller, not the next buyer.

This lesson examines a key ruling in Hanafi fiqh regarding the sale of goods that are customarily measured or weighed. When a buyer purchases such goods after taking measurement or weight, then wishes to resell them by the same unit, the Hanafi school requires a fresh measurement or weight for the new buyer. This requirement is not a mere formality; it is a safeguard against fraud and ensures the new buyer receives the exact quantity. We will explore the textual proofs from the Quran and Sunnah that ground this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Identify the specific transaction: a buyer purchases a makil or mawzun item by measure/weight, takes possession, then sells it by measure/weight. The ruling: it is not permissible (la yajuz) to resell by measure/weight without re-measuring/re-weighing. The second sale is invalid (batil) if done without re-measurement.
The ruling only applies when the second sale is by measure/weight, not by lump sum (jizaf).
2
Locate the dalil
The passage cites three proofs: Quran 83:3 (condemning giving less measure), a hadith from Uthman (when you sell, measure; when you buy, measure), and a hadith from Jabir (food must pass two measures: seller's and buyer's).
The first two proofs emphasize full measurement; the third directly requires two measures for food resale.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
For the Quran: the verse implies the obligation of full measure, and by extension, the seller must ensure the buyer's measure is accurate. For the hadiths: the command to measure when selling indicates that measurement is integral to a valid sale by measure; the hadith of Jabir explicitly requires two measures, meaning the buyer must re-measure before reselling.
The author notes that the hadith of Jabir makes re-measuring recommended (mustahabb) at the time of eating, but obligatory when reselling by measure/weight.
4
Note the exception
If the second sale is by lump sum (jizaf), without specifying exact measure/weight, then re-measuring/re-weighing is not required. This is because no specific quantity is promised, so the risk of fraud is absent.
This exception is derived from the general principle of giving full measure; when the sale is jizaf, the buyer accepts the goods as they are.
5
Identify the learned principles
The ruling is based on the principle of preventing gharar (uncertainty/fraud) and the obligation to give full measure and weight. The re-measurement ensures the new buyer has certainty about the quantity.
This is a condition (shart) for the validity of the second sale by measure/weight.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۹۲۵] (۱۱) کسی نے کیلی چیز کیل کر کے خریدی یا وزنی چیز وزن کر کے خریدی پھر اس کو کیل کیا یا وزن کیا پھر اس کو کیل سے یا وزن سے بیچا تو مشتری کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ اس کو نیچے اور نہ یہ جائز ہے کہ اس کو کھائے یہاں تک کہ دوبارہ کیل یا وزن کر لے۔ کیلی چیز مثلا گیہوں چاول اور وزنی چیز مثلا درہم اور دنا نیر کیل اور وزن سے خریدا۔ اور کیل یا وزن کر کے بائع سے لیا۔ اب اس کو دو بارہ کیل کر کے یا وزن کر کے بیچنا چاہتا ہے انکل سے نہیں تو پہلا کیل کیا ہو یا وزن کیا ہوا کافی نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ اگلے مشتری کے سامنے دوبارہ کیل کرنا ہوگا۔ یا وزنی چیز ہے تو وزن کرنا ہوگا۔
حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا جس نے غلہ بیچا تو اس کو نہ بیچے یہاں تک کہ اس کو پورا لے لے ، راوی اسمعیل نے یہ بھی فرمایا کہ اس کو نہ بیچے جب تک کہ اس پر قبضہ نہ کرنے (ب) بہر حال جس سے حضور نے روکا ہے وہ غلہ جات ہیں کہ قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے بیچا جائے (ج) حضرت ابن سیرین نے فرمایا کوئی حرج نہیں ہے کہ آدمی کوئی ایسی چیز خریدے جو نہ کیل کی جاتی ہو اور نہ وزن کی جاتی ہو نقد کے ذریعہ پھر اس کو قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے بیچے۔
(۱) پہلا کیل کرنا یا وزن کرنا پہلے مشتری کو حوالے کرنے کے لئے تھا۔ یہ وزن اگلے مشتری کے لئے کافی نہیں ہے۔ اگر کیل یا وزن سے اس نے خریدا ہے تو اس کے سامنے دوبارہ کیل یا وزن کرنا ہوگا۔ تا کہ اس کو اطمینان ہو۔ اور کمی زیادتی نہ ہونے پائے (۲) آیت میں اس کی تاکید ہے الذين اذا اكتالوا على الناس يستوفون واذا كاكالوهم او وزنوهم يخسرون (الف) ( آیت ۳/۲ سورة المط ۸۳) اس آیت میں کیل اور وزن پورا دینے کی تاکید ہے (۳) حدیث میں ہے عن عثمان ان النبي الله قال اذا بعت فكل واذا ابتعت فاکتل (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب الکیل علی البائع والمعطى ص ۲۸۵ نمبر ۲۱۲۶ ر مسلم شریف ، باب بطلان بیع المبيع قبل القبض ص ۵ نمبر ۱۵۲۸) (۳) ابن ماجہ شریف میں ہے عن جابر قال نهى رسول الله الله عن بيع الطعام حتى يجرى فيه الضاعان صاع البائع وصاع المشترى (ج) ابن ماجہ شریف، باب النھی عن بنج الطعام قبل مالم يقبض ص ۱۳۱۹ نمبر ۲۲۲۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مشتری جب تک دوبارہ کیل نہ کرے اگلے مشتری کو نہ بیچے۔ نوٹ اس حدیث کی بنیاد پر کھانے کے وقت دوبارہ کیل کرنا استحبابی ہے۔ کیونکہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ غلہ زیادہ آ گیا ہو تو بائع کو واپس کر سکے، یا کم آیا ہو تو اس سے لے سکے۔
و اگر کیل یاوزن کر کے نہ بیچے بلکہ انکل سے بیچے تو دوبارہ کیل کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ کسی کو مال پور ا دینا چاہیئے اور پورا لینا چاہئے۔ اسی اصول پر یہ مسئلہ متفرع ہے۔
[925] (11) If someone buys a measured item by measurement, or a weighed item by weight, then measures or weighs it, and then sells it by measurement or weight, it is not permissible for the buyer from whom he purchased to sell it nor to eat it until he re-measures or re-weighs it. For example, measured items like wheat and rice, and weighed items like dirhams and dinars, purchased by measurement or weight. And he took it after measuring or weighing. Now he wants to sell it by measure or weight, not by lump sum. Then the first measurement or weighing is not sufficient. Rather, he must re-measure or re-weigh in front of the next buyer. Footnote: (a) The Prophet said: 'He who sold grain should not sell it until he takes full possession.' (b) Whatever the Prophet forbade is grain to be sold before possession. (c) Ibn Sirin said: 'There is no harm in a person buying something that is not measured or weighed for cash and then selling it before possession.' (1) The first measurement or weighing was for handing over to the first buyer. That measurement is not sufficient for the next buyer. If the sale is by measure or weight, then re-measurement or re-weighing must be done in his presence to ensure no deficiency or excess. (2) The Quran emphasizes: 'Those who, when they take a measure from people, take it fully, but when they give measure or weight, give less.' This verse emphasizes giving full measure and weight. (3) Hadith from Uthman: The Prophet said: 'When you sell, measure; when you buy, measure.' (Bukhari, Muslim). (3) In Ibn Majah: 'The Prophet forbade selling food until two measures pass through it: the seller's measure and the buyer's measure.' This hadith indicates that the buyer must re-measure before resale. Note: On the basis of this hadith, re-measuring at the time of eating is recommended (mustahabb) because it may be that more came, so he can return it to the seller, or less came, so he can take from him. And if he sells not by measure or weight but by lump sum (jizaf), then re-measuring is not required. One should give full property and take full property. On this principle this issue is based.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage deals with a specific ruling in the Hanafi school regarding the sale of goods that are customarily sold by measure (makilat) or weight (mawzunat). When a person buys such goods and takes possession after measuring or weighing, then wishes to resell them by the same measure or weight, he is required to re-measure or re-weigh them in front of the new buyer. The first measurement, which was done for the first seller, does not suffice. The reason is to ensure transparency and prevent fraud, as the new buyer has the right to see the exact quantity. The author cites Quranic verse (Surah al-Mutaffifin, 83:3) emphasizing full measure, and two hadiths: one commanding measurement when selling and buying, and another from Ibn Majah stating that food should not be sold until two measures pass (the seller's and the buyer's). However, if the sale is made by lump sum (jizaf), without specifying the exact measure, then re-measuring is not required because the buyer accepts it as is. The author notes that re-measuring at the time of consumption is recommended (mustahabb) based on the hadith, but it becomes obligatory when the sale is by measure or weight. This ruling is derived from the general principle of giving full measure and avoiding fraud.

Key Terms
مكيل (makil): Something sold by volume measurement (e.g., wheat, rice).
موزون (mawzun): Something sold by weight measurement (e.g., gold, silver, or goods sold by weight).
جزاف (jizaf): Selling by lump sum without exact measurement or weight.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The sale is valid because the first weighing suffices.
B) The sale is invalid because re-weighing is required.
C) The sale is permissible but makruh.
D) The buyer may eat it but not sell it.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, re-measuring or re-weighing before resale by measure/weight is a condition for validity, based on the Quranic command for full measure and prophetic practice.

Disposing of the Price Before Taking Possession
Ruling that buyer may use price before qabd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on disposing of the price before qabd and explain the distinction between price as dayn and as 'ayn.

Core Idea
The price remains a debt (dayn) until paid – the buyer may use it freely before qabd.

This passage addresses a practical question: once a sale is concluded, can the buyer use the agreed price (e.g., spend or gift it) before actually handing it to the seller? The Hanafi school draws a sharp line between the price being a general debt (dayn) and a specific object ('ayn). Here, the author explains why, unless the price is a specific item, the buyer can dispose of it before possession, citing a tradition from Ibn Sirin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Locate the core legal statement: 'it is permissible to dispose of the price before taking possession.' Note the hukm level – ja'iz (permissible).
2
Find the key distinction
The passage distinguishes between price as a general debt and price as a specific 'ayn. Determine why this distinction matters for the permissibility of disposal before qabd.
The price is not specified by mere mention in the contract.
3
Analyze the proof (dalil)
Examine the tradition from Ibn Sirin: when you sell for a dinar, you may take anything equivalent in type or otherwise. This shows the price is not a specific object.
The tradition supports that the price remains unspecified and thus can be fulfilled with similar items.
4
Apply the exception
Recognize the exception: if the price is a specific commodity (e.g., a particular car), then it becomes 'ayn and cannot be disposed of before qabd.
This exception is hinted at in the last line: 'the proofs have passed earlier.'
5
Connect to wider Hanafi principle
Relate this to the principle that a debt (dayn) is not tied to a specific object; it is a liability in the buyer's responsibility until paid. Thus, the buyer may use his own funds before payment.
This aligns with the Hanafi view that the price is not a property of the seller until qabd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۹۲۶] (۱۲) اور تصرف کرنا شمن میں قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے جائز ہے۔ ر بائع نے بیچنے کی ابھی بات کی ہے اور بیچ دی تھی لیکن مشتری نے ابھی ثمن نہیں دیا ہے اور نہ بائع نے اس پر قبضہ کیا ہے۔ اس سے پہلے اس شمن کے ذریعہ کوئی چیز خریدنا چاہے تو خرید سکتا ہے۔ یا شمن کو ہبہ کرنا چاہے تو ہبہ کرسکتا ہے۔ شمن متعین کرنے سے متعین نہیں ہوتا اس لئے یہ ثمن نہیں دے سکے گا تو اپنی طرف سے کوئی دوسرا پونڈ یا روپیہ دے دے گا۔ یہی شمن دینا کوئی ضروری نہیں ہے۔ اس شمن کی تعین تو بائع کو بھروسہ دینے کے لئے کی ہے۔ اثر میں ہے کہ یمن کے بدلے کوئی اور چیز بھی لے سکتا ہے۔ عن ابن سيرين قال اذا بعت شيئا بدينار فحل الاجل فخذ بالدينار ما شئت من ذلك النوع و غیره (و)(مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب المسلمة يسلمها فی دینا ر هل يأخذ غیر الدینارج نامن ص ۱۶ نمبر ۱۴۱۱۶) اس اثر میں ہے کہ ثمن دینار ہو تو اس کے بدلے کوئی اور چیز لے سکتا ہے۔ جس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ ثمن متعین کرنے سے متعین نہیں ہوتا۔ اس لئے اس کو قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے تصرف کر سکتا ہے۔
شمن اگر سامان ہے جو متعین کرنے سے متعین ہوتا ہے اس پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے پیچ نہیں سکتا ۔ دلائل پہلے گزر چکے ہیں۔
حاشیہ : (الف) وہ لوگ جو لوگوں سے کیل کر کے لیتے ہیں تو پورا لیتے ہیں۔ اور جب کیل کر کے دیتے ہیں یا وزن کر کے دیتے ہیں تو کم دیتے ہیں (ب ) آپ نے فرمایا جب بچو تو کیل کر کے بیچو اور جب خرید و تو کیل کرو (ج) آپ نے غلوں کو بیچنے سے روکا یہاں تک کہ اس میں دو صاع جاری ہوں، بائع کا صاع اور مشتری کا صاع ( د ) ابن سیرین نے فرمایا اگر آپ نے کسی چیز کو دینار کے بدلے بیچا پس وقت آیا تو دینار کے بدلے جو چاہے لواسی قسم میں سے یا اس کے علاوہ۔
[926] (12) And it is permissible to dispose of the price before taking possession. The seller has already spoken about selling and has sold, but the buyer has not yet given the price, nor has the seller taken possession of it. Before that, if he wants to buy something with this price, he can buy; or if he wants to gift the price, he can gift it. The price is not specified by being named; therefore, if he cannot give this very price, he will give another pound or rupee. It is not necessary to give the same price. Its specification is only to give confidence to the seller. There is a tradition: from Ibn Sirin that he said: 'If you sold something for a dinar and the term comes, then take from the dinar whatever you wish of that type or other.' This shows that the price is not specified. Therefore, he can dispose of it before taking possession. If the price is a specific commodity that is specified by naming, then it cannot be sold before taking possession; the proofs have passed earlier. Footnotes: (a) Those who take measure from people take full, but when they give measure or weight, they give less. (b) The Prophet said: 'When you sell, measure; when you buy, measure.' (c) The Prophet forbade selling grains until two measures pass: the seller's and the buyer's. (d) Ibn Sirin said: 'If you sold something for a dinar and the time comes, take for the dinar whatever you wish of that type or otherwise.'
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage discusses the permissibility of the buyer disposing of the price (thaman) before physically taking possession of it from the seller. The key distinction is that the price, when it is general (like a debt or a sum of money), is not considered a specific 'ayn (specific object) that becomes determined by specification in the contract. Therefore, the buyer can use it for other transactions, such as buying something else or gifting it, before actually paying it to the seller. This is because if the buyer cannot provide the exact price, he can provide a similar amount. The author cites a tradition from Ibn Sirin that if you sell something for a dinar, you can take anything equivalent to that dinar. However, if the price is a specific commodity that becomes 'ayn (like a specific item), then it cannot be disposed of before qabd, as the earlier proofs indicate. The footnotes reiterate the Quranic and hadith emphasis on full measure, which are more relevant to the previous lesson. This ruling is an example of the Hanafi principle that the price in a sale contract is not a specific property until it is paid and taken possession.

Key Terms
ثمن (thaman): The price given in exchange for the purchased item.
قبض (qabd): Taking physical possession. For price, it means the seller actually receiving the money.
عين ('ayn): A specific, tangible object that is determined by its identity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is it permissible for a buyer to dispose of the price before taking possession from the seller?
A) Because the price is not a specific object until it is paid.
B) Because the seller has given permission in the contract.
C) Because the buyer is the owner of the price.
D) Because the price is considered a debt.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the price in a sale remains a debt (dayn) until paid, so the buyer may dispose of it freely before physical possession, unless the price is a specific 'ayn.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate

Disposal of Price Before Possession
Ruling on buyer's disposal of price before possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on disposal of price before possession and explain the proofs and the distinction between thaman as dayn and 'ayn.

Core Idea
The price in a sale is a debt (dayn), not a specific item, so the buyer may dispose of it before possession.

In a sale, does the buyer own the price in a specific sense the moment it is named? The Hanafi school says no – the price remains a liability until it is paid. This has practical consequences: the buyer can use the money elsewhere before handing it over. In this lesson, we examine the ruling, its proofs, and how it differs from the Shafi'i position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and key terms
The passage states: 'التصرف في الثمن قبل القبض جائز.' Identify the act (tasarruf fi al-thaman), the condition (qabl al-qabd), and the ruling (ja'iz/permissible).
2
Understand the nature of thaman as dayn
The text explains that the price is not determined by specification (ta'yin). It is a debt in the buyer's liability. Contrast this with a specific commodity (thaman 'ayn) which becomes determined and cannot be disposed of before possession.
3
Examine the proofs
The passage cites the Quranic verse from Surah al-Mutaffifin, hadith from Uthman (measure when selling), hadith from Jabir (both measures for food), and an athar from Ibn Sirin allowing substitution of the price. How does each support the ruling?
4
Compare with Shafi'i position
The Shafi'i school analogizes price to a specific commodity, requiring possession before disposal. Identify the thamarah al-khilaf: the practical consequence in daily transactions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

چاہیے اور پورا لینا چاہیے۔ اسی اصول پر یہ مسئلہ متفرع ہے۔ (۹۲۶) (۱۲) اور تصرف کرنا ثمن میں قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے جائز ہے۔ ر بائع نے بیچنے کی ابھی بات کی ہے اور بیچ دی تھی لیکن مشتری نے ابھی ثمن نہیں دیا ابن سيرين قال اذا بعت شيئا بدينار فحل الاجل فخذ بالدينار ما شئت من ذلك النوع و غیره (و) (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب المسلمۃ یسلمہا فی دینار ہل یأخذ غیر الدینار ج ۸ ص ۱۶ نمبر ۱۴۱۱۶) اس اثر میں ہے کہ ثمن اس پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے بیچ نہیں سکتا۔ دلائل پہلے گزر چکے ہیں۔ حاشیہ : (الف) وہ لوگ جو لوگوں سے کیل کر کے لیتے ہیں تو پورا لیتے ہیں۔ اور جب کیل کر کے دیتے ہیں یا وزن کر کے دیتے ہیں تو کم دیتے ہیں (ب ) آپ نے فرمایا جب بیچو تو کیل کر کے بیچو اور جب خرید و تو کیل کرو (ج) آپ نے غلے کو بیچنے سے روکا یہاں تک کہ اس میں دو صاع جاری ہوں، بائع کا صاع اور مشتری کا صاع ( د ) ابن سیرین نے فرمایا اگر آپ نے کسی چیز کو دینار کے بدلے بیچا پس وقت آیا تو دینار کے بدلے جو چاہے لو اسی قسم میں سے یا اس کے علاوہ۔
And disposal of the price before possession is permissible. (1) The first measuring or weighing was for handing over to the first buyer. That weighing is not sufficient for the next buyer. If he bought by measure or weight, then he must re-measure or re-weigh in his presence, so that he is satisfied and no increase or decrease occurs. (2) The verse emphasizes this: 'Those who, when they take measure from people, take full measure, and when they give measure or weight, they give less' (Surah al-Mutaffifin 83:1-3). (3) The hadith: from Uthman that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'When you sell, measure; and when you buy, measure' (Bukhari, Muslim). (3) In Ibn Majah: from Jabir: 'The Messenger of Allah forbade selling food until both measures are used: the measure of the seller and the measure of the buyer' (Ibn Majah). Note: Based on this hadith, re-measuring at the time of taking food is recommended, because it may be that the grain is more, so he can return it to the seller, or less, so he can take from him. And if he does not sell by measure or weight but sells by a heap, then there is no need to re-measure. One should give full property and take full. This issue is derived from this principle. (926) (12) And disposal of the price before possession is permissible. The seller has only spoken of selling and sold, but the buyer has not yet given the price and the seller has not taken possession of it. Before that, if he wishes to buy something with that price, he can buy; or if he wishes to give the price as a gift, he can give it. The price is not determined by specification, so if he cannot give that price, he will give another pound or rupee from his side. It is not necessary to give the same price. The specification of this price is only to give confidence to the seller. There is an athar: from Ibn Sirin: 'When you sell something for a dinar and the term comes, take whatever you wish of that type or other than it' (Musannaf Abdur Razzaq). This athar indicates that if the price is a dinar, one can take something else in exchange. The meaning is that the price is not determined by specification. Therefore, one can dispose of it before taking possession. If the price is a commodity, which is determined by specification, then one cannot sell it before taking possession. The proofs for this have passed before. Footnotes: (a) Those who take measure from people take full measure, and when they give measure or weight, they give less. (b) He said: When you sell, measure; and when you buy, measure. (c) He forbade selling grains until both measures are used: the seller's measure and the buyer's measure. (d) Ibn Sirin said: If you sell something for a dinar and the term comes, take whatever you wish of that type or other than it.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that the buyer may dispose of the price (thaman) before taking physical possession (qabd) of it. The reasoning is that the price is not considered 'determined' (mu'ayyan) merely by specifying it in the contract; rather, it remains a debt or obligation in the buyer's liability (dhimmah). Therefore, the buyer can use that price to buy something else or give it as a gift, and if he fails to deliver the specified price, he can substitute it with another equivalent. The text supports this with several evidences: (1) A verse from Surah al-Mutaffifin emphasizing fairness in measurement, implying that the seller should get full measure; (2) A hadith from Uthman commanding to measure when selling and buying; (3) Another hadith from Jabir requiring both the seller's and buyer's measures for food sales; and (4) An athar from Ibn Sirin allowing substitution of the price. The commentary also distinguishes between price that is a fungible (e.g., currency) and price that is a specific commodity. For fungible prices, disposal before possession is allowed; for specific commodities, it is not, because specific commodities become determined by specification and cannot be disposed of before possession. This is a core issue in Hanafi fiqh regarding the nature of the thaman and its legal status.

Key Terms
ثمن (thaman): The price or consideration in a sale; it can be fungible (currency) or specific (commodity).
قبض (qabd): Taking physical possession or control of an item; for currency, it is not required for validity of disposal.
تصرف (tasarruf): Legal disposition, such as selling, gifting, or using the price before paying it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is it permissible for the buyer to dispose of the price before taking possession?
A) Because the price is not specified in the contract.
B) Because the price is considered a debt (dayn) in the buyer's liability, not a specific item.
C) Because the seller has given permission.
D) Because the buyer must pay at a later date.

Key Takeaway
The price is a debt, not a specific good; hence disposal before possession is allowed.

Buyer May Increase Price
Ruling with proof from Sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a buyer voluntarily increasing the agreed price and identify the hadith evidence that supports its permissibility.

Core Idea
A buyer may voluntarily give more than the agreed price; it is permissible and commendable.

This lesson examines a simple yet important ruling in Islamic commercial ethics: the permissibility of a buyer voluntarily giving more than the agreed price. While contracts are binding, the Hanafi school teaches that a buyer's voluntary increase, done out of goodwill, is not only allowed but commended. The source passage cites the Prophet's practice as proof, showing that generosity in repayment is a praiseworthy trait.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what the source is ruling on: the buyer voluntarily adding to the agreed price. The ruling is stated as 'ja'iz' (permissible).
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
Find the proof cited in the source: the hadith from Abu Rafi' where the Prophet borrowed a young camel and returned a better one.
The hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the evidence proves the ruling)
Analyze how the hadith supports the ruling. The Prophet's act of returning a better camel is a voluntary increase, and he praised good repayment. This shows that such increase is praiseworthy and allowed.
The key phrase: 'the best of people are those who are best in repayment.'
4
Note ikhtilaf (scholarly disagreement)
Check if there is any disagreement. The source indicates no intra-Hanafi or inter-madhhab dispute; the ruling is 'muttafaq alayh' (agreed upon).
All schools agree on the permissibility of voluntary increase by the debtor.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred position)
Since there is no conflict, the mufta bihi (operative ruling) is simply that the increase is permissible and commendable.
Authority weight: zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز للمشترى ان يزيد البائع فى الثمن (۱۳) اور مشتری کے لئے جائز ہے کہ بائع کو ثمن میں زیادہ دے۔ مثلا دس پونڈ میں کپڑا خریدا ہے اب مشتری خوش ہو کر بارہ پونڈ دینا چاہتا ہے تو دے سکتا ہے۔ یہ مشتری کی ملکیت ہے اس کو جیسا چاہے خرچ کر سکتا ہے (۲) حدیث میں قیمت زیادہ دی گئی ہے۔ عن ابی رافع قال استسلف رسول الله بكرا فجاءته ابل من الصدقة فامرنى ان اقضى الرجل بكرة فقلت لم اجد في الابل الا جملا خيارا رباعيا فقال النبي اعطه اياه فان خيار الناس احسنهم قضاء (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی حسن القضاء ص ۱۹ نمبر ۳۳۴۶) اس حدیث میں جوان اونٹ لیا تھا اور اس کے بدلے اچھے قسم کا اونٹ واپس دیا اور فرمایا کہ حسن ادا کرنے والا اچھا آدمی ہے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ مشتری زیادہ دینا چاہے تو دے سکتا ہے۔
And it is permissible for the buyer to increase the price to the seller. (13) It is permissible for the buyer to give more to the seller in the price. For example, he bought cloth for ten pounds; now the buyer, being happy, wants to give twelve pounds, so he can give it. This is the buyer's property; he can spend it as he wishes. (2) In the hadith, the price was increased: from Abu Rafi' that the Messenger of Allah borrowed a young camel, then camels from sadaqah came to him, so he ordered me to pay the man a young camel. I said: I did not find among the camels except a good four-year-old camel. The Prophet said: Give it to him, for the best of people are those who are best in repayment. (Abu Dawood). In this hadith, he had taken a young camel and returned a better one, and he said that the one who repays well is a good person. From this it is understood that if the buyer wants to give more, he can do so.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. It states that the buyer voluntarily giving more than the agreed price to the seller is permissible (ja'iz). The buyer owns his property and may spend it as he wishes. The proof is a hadith from Abu Rafi' where the Prophet (peace be upon him) borrowed a young camel and returned a better one, praising good repayment. This indicates that giving more is commendable but not obligatory. The text also mentions that the buyer does this willingly (khush hokar). There is no mention of any condition or restriction; it is simply permissible.

Key Terms
زيادة (ziyadah): Voluntary addition to the agreed price by the buyer.
قضاء (qada'): Repayment or settlement of a debt; in the hadith, good qada' is praised.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling if a buyer voluntarily gives more than the agreed price to the seller?
A) It is haram because it changes the contract.
B) It is permissible and commendable.
C) It is makruh because it resembles riba.
D) It is valid only if the seller agrees.

Key Takeaway
A buyer may voluntarily increase the price after a sale; it is permissible and commendable, based on the Prophet's example of good repayment.

Voluntary Increase or Discount by Seller
Ruling allowing seller to voluntarily increase goods or reduce price

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a seller voluntarily increasing goods or reducing price, and identify the hadith proof and its implication.

Core Idea
A seller may voluntarily give extra goods or discount; it is permissible and commendable.

In Islamic commercial transactions, generosity is encouraged. The Hanafi school affirms that a seller, being the owner, may voluntarily increase the quantity of the sold item or reduce the agreed price after the contract. This lesson examines the ruling and its proof from the Sunnah, highlighting that such acts are not obligatory but are meritorious.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the seller voluntarily increasing the sold item (ziyadah fi al-mabi') or reducing the price (hatt min al-thaman). The ruling is 'ja'iz' (permissible) and it is also mustahabb (recommended) due to the hadith.
The text uses 'yajuz' which indicates permissibility.
2
Understand the rationale of ownership
The seller is the owner of the goods and the price; he may dispose of his property as he wishes, provided it does not violate any prohibition. Thus, adding extra or discounting is his right.
This is based on the general principle of ownership.
3
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Suwayd ibn Qays in Abu Dawood: The Prophet (peace be upon him) told a man weighing goods to 'Weigh and give extra' (zan wa arjih). This hadith is a proof for the permissibility and desirability.
Hadith is ahad, but its meaning is supported by general principles.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'arjih' (give extra) is an imperative indicating permissibility and recommendation, not obligation. The context shows the Prophet encouraged voluntary generosity in transactions.
In Hanafi usul, a command may indicate wujub or nadb depending on context. Here it indicates nadb.
5
Note the cross-madhhab status
This ruling is muttafaq alayh (agreed upon) among the four schools. There is no significant dispute; all schools consider it permissible and commendable.
Thus the lesson is straightforward without ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز للبائع ان يزيد في المبيع ويجوز ان يحط من الثمن (۱۴) اور بائع کے لئے جائز ہے کہ مبیع میں زیادہ کر دے اور جائز ہے کہ ثمن میں کمی کر دے۔ بائع کے لئے یہ بھی جائز ہے کہ جتنی مبیع طے ہوئی ہے اس سے زیادہ دے اور یہ بھی جائز ہے کہ جتنا ثمن طے ہوا ہے اس سے کم لے۔ اس کی ملکیت ہے وہ ایسا کر سکتا ہے (۲) مبیع زیادہ دینے کی ترغیب حدیث میں ہے۔ حدثنا سويد بن قيس ... ولم رجل يزن بالاجر فقال له رسول الله زن و ارجح (ب) ( ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی الرجحان فی الوزن ص ۱۸ نمبر ۳۳۳۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بائع کو چاہئے کہ مبیع کو وزن میں کچھ زیادہ ہی دینا چاہئے۔
And it is permissible for the seller to increase in the sold item and it is permissible for him to reduce from the price. (14) It is permissible for the seller to give more in the sold item and it is permissible to reduce the price. The seller may give more than the agreed quantity of sold goods and also may take less than the agreed price. It is his property, he can do so. (2) There is encouragement in hadith to give more of the sold item: Suwayd ibn Qays narrated... a man was weighing with a wage and the Messenger of Allah said to him: 'Weigh and give extra.' (Abu Dawood). This hadith indicates that the seller should give a little extra in weight.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. It allows the seller to voluntarily increase the quantity of the sold item (mabi') or reduce the price (thaman). The seller is the owner and may be generous. The proof is a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) told a weigher to 'weigh and give extra' (zan wa arjih). This shows the commendable nature of giving extra. The text clarifies that both actions are ja'iz (permissible) and the seller may do so out of his own will. There is no obligation; it is a voluntary act of kindness.

Key Terms
زيادة في المبيع (ziyadah fi al-mabi'): Voluntary increase in the quantity or quality of the sold item by the seller.
حط (hatt): Reduction or discount given by the seller from the agreed price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith mentioned, how should a seller weigh goods?
A) Exactly as agreed, no more or less.
B) Weigh and give extra (arzih).
C) Weigh and take payment first.
D) Weigh in the presence of witnesses.

Key Takeaway
A seller may voluntarily increase the goods or reduce the price after sale; it is permissible and recommended, supported by the Prophet's instruction to weigh and give extra.

Effect of Voluntary Adjustments on Subsequent Rights
Ruling that entitlements attach to the final adjusted price/goods

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain what happens to rights like murābaḥah, tawliyah, and shuf'ah when the buyer or seller voluntarily adjusts the price or quantity in a sale.

Core Idea
A voluntary price adjustment becomes the new basis for all subsequent rights.

In Hanafi fiqh, when either party to a sale voluntarily changes the price or quantity of goods, that adjustment does not merely stand as an independent act; it amends the original contract terms. All legal entitlements that depend on the contract, such as the cost disclosure in murābaḥah or the calculation of shuf'ah, must now be based on the final adjusted figures. This lesson explores the principle and its application to real transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle
Understand that voluntary adjustments to price or quantity change the basis for all subsequent rights. The text states: 'entitlement attaches to all.'
The adjustment must be voluntary; forced changes may have different effects.
2
Examine the First Example
When the buyer pays more than the original price, the excess paid becomes the new cost basis. Thus murābaḥah and tawliyah are calculated on the higher amount.
This applies whether the buyer pays 12 instead of 10, or any other increase.
3
Examine the Second Example
When the seller gives more goods for the same price, the buyer's cost basis is the total goods received for that price. The buyer must state: 'I bought two items for ten pounds' instead of one.
Similar logic: the actual transaction defines the cost.
4
Examine the Third Example and Shuf'ah
When the seller reduces the price, the buyer's cost is the reduced amount. The person claiming shuf'ah must claim it based on the current (adjusted) price and goods.
All rights (murābaḥah, tawliyah, shuf'ah) follow the final terms.
5
Derive the Underlying Reasoning
The voluntary adjustment effectively amends the original contract. The new price or quantity becomes the 'original' for legal purposes, so all entitlements depend on it.
This is a general Hanafi rule, not limited to the examples given.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويتعلق الاستحقاق بجميع (۱۵) اور استحقاق ان تمام کے ساتھ متعلق ہوں گے۔ مثلا مشتری نے دس پونڈ قیمت کی تھی اس کے بجائے بارہ پونڈ دیے تو اب مرابحہ اور تولیہ جو کرے گا وہ بارہ پونڈ پر کرے گا۔ اسی طرح بائع نے ایک مبیع کے بجائے دو مبیع دس پونڈ میں دیدی تو اب یوں کہے گا کہ دو مبیع دس پونڈ میں لی ہیں۔ یوں نہیں کہے گا کہ ایک مبیع دس پونڈ میں لی ہے۔ اسی طرح بائع نے دس پونڈ کے بجائے آٹھ پونڈ لئے تو لینے والا یوں کہے گا کہ آٹھ پونڈ میں مبیع خریدی ہے۔ اور اسی آٹھ پونڈ پر مرابحہ اور تولیہ کرے گا۔ اب دس پونڈ پر مرابحہ یا تولیہ نہیں کرے گا۔ اسی طرح جو آدمی شفعہ کا دعوی کرے گا وہ اب موجودہ قیمت اور موجودہ بیع پر شفعہ کا دعوی کرے گا۔ کیونکہ اب یہی قیمت اصل بن گئی اور زیادہ دی ہوئی قیمت یا بائع کی جانب سے کم کی ہوئی قیمت ہی اصل بن گئی۔ اس لئے اب تمام حقوق اسی پر منحصر ہوں گے۔
And entitlement (istiḥqāq) attaches to all. (15) And entitlements will relate to all of them. For example, the buyer had priced at ten pounds; instead he gave twelve pounds, then when he does murābaḥah or tawliyah, he will do so on the basis of twelve pounds. Similarly, if the seller gave two items instead of one for ten pounds, then he will say: I bought two items for ten pounds; he will not say that I bought one item for ten pounds. Similarly, if the seller took eight pounds instead of ten, the buyer will say: I bought the item for eight pounds, and he will do murābaḥah and tawliyah on the basis of those eight pounds; he will not do murābaḥah or tawliyah on ten pounds. Similarly, the person who claims shuf'ah will claim shuf'ah on the current price and the current sale. Because now this price has become the original, and the increased price or the reduced price by the seller has become the original. Therefore, all rights now depend on this.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This is a ruling that explains the legal effect of voluntary adjustments by buyer or seller. When either party voluntarily changes the price or quantity, the adjusted figures become the new basis for any subsequent legal claims or transactions (such as murābaḥah, tawliyah, and shuf'ah). The text gives three examples: (1) If the buyer pays 12 instead of 10, any resale with profit disclosure (murābaḥah) or at cost (tawliyah) must be calculated on the actual 12 paid. (2) If the seller gives two items instead of one for the same price, the buyer's cost basis is two items for that price. (3) If the seller reduces the price from 10 to 8, the buyer's cost is 8. Similarly, the right of pre-emption (shuf'ah) is determined based on the final consideration in the sale. The underlying principle is that the voluntàry increase or decrease effectively amends the original contract terms, and all subsequent rights attach to the amended terms.

Key Terms
استحقاق (istiḥqāq): Entitlement or right that arises from the sale, such as the right to claim shuf'ah or the right to disclose cost in murābaḥah.
مرابحہ (murābaḥah): A sale where the seller discloses the cost and adds a profit margin.
شفعہ (shuf'ah): The right of pre-emption, allowing a co-owner or neighbor to buy the share sold to a third party.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a buyer voluntarily pays 12 pounds for an item originally priced at 10 pounds, what will be the basis for a murābaḥah sale?
A) 10 pounds, because that was the original agreement.
B) 12 pounds, because that is what the buyer actually paid.
C) The market value at the time of murābaḥah.
D) The average of 10 and 12.

Key Takeaway
Voluntary adjustments to price or quantity redefine the contract's terms for all legal purposes, including murābaḥah, tawliyah, and shuf'ah.

Buyer's Voluntary Price Increase: Permissibility and Proof
Ruling with proof: voluntary price increase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a buyer voluntarily increasing the price and explain the hadith evidence for its permissibility.

Core Idea
A buyer may voluntarily give extra to the seller; it is a praiseworthy act of generosity.

In sales, once a price is agreed, is it permissible for the buyer to pay more voluntarily? This lesson addresses that question. We will examine the ruling, its basis in a prophetic hadith, and why it is considered a virtuous act rather than a contractual requirement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the first sentence: 'ويجوز للمشترى ان يزيد البائع فى الثمن' — 'It is permissible for the buyer to increase the price for the seller.' Note the ruling is ja'iz (permissible).
2
Understand the example
The text gives a concrete example: a buyer purchased cloth for £10 and later wants to give £12. This illustrates that the buyer is giving from his own property voluntarily.
3
Analyze the dalil
The hadith from Abu Dawud is cited. Abu Rafi' was ordered to repay a borrowed camel with a young camel, but only a superior camel was available. The Prophet allowed giving the better camel, saying the best people are best in repayment.
The proof is that giving extra is praiseworthy and not prohibited.
4
Confirm the legal status
The commentary emphasizes that this is not obligatory but a voluntary generosity. The ruling is mubah (permissible) and mustahab (recommended) by implication.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(١٣) ويجوز للمشترى ان يزيد البائع فى الثمن اور مشتری کے لئے جائز ہے کہ بائع کو شمن میں زیادہ دے۔ مثلا دس پونڈ میں کپڑا خریدا ہے اب مشتری خوش ہو کر بارہ پونڈ دینا چاہتا ہے تو دے سکتا ہے۔ یہ مشتری کی ملکیت ہے اس کو جیسا چاہے خرچ کر سکتا ہے (۲) حدیث میں قیمت زیادہ دی گئی ہے۔ عن ابی رافع قال استسلف رسول الله بكرا فجائته ابل من الصدقة فامر نى ان اقضى الرجل بكرة فقلت لم اجد في الابل الا جملا خيارا رباعيا فقال النبي له اعطه اياه فان خيار الناس احسنهم قضاء (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی حسن القضاء ص ۱۹ نمبر ۳۳۴۶) اس حدیث میں جوان اونٹ لیا تھا اور اس کے بدلے اچھے قسم کا اونٹ واپس دیا اور فرمایا کہ حسن ادا کرنے والا اچھا آدمی ہے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ مشتری زیادہ دینا چاہے تو دے سکتا ہے۔ حاشیہ : (الف) حضور نے جوان اونٹ کا سودا کیا پھر آپ کے پاس صدقہ کا اونٹ آیا تو مجھے حضور نے حکم دیا کہ جوان اونٹ ادا کردوں تو میں اونٹ میں نہیں پایا مگر اس سے اچھا اونٹ چار دانت والا ۔ آپ نے فرمایا کہ اچھا اونٹ اس کو دیدو۔ اچھے لوگ وہ ہیں جو اچھے انداز سے ادا کرے
And it is permissible for the buyer to increase the price for the seller. For example, he bought a cloth for ten pounds, now the buyer, being pleased, wants to give twelve pounds, so he may give it. This is the buyer's property, he may spend it as he wishes. (2) There is a hadith about increasing the price: From Abu Rafi', he said: The Messenger of Allah borrowed a young camel, then camels from charity came to him, so he ordered me to repay the man a young camel. I said: I did not find among the camels except a superior four-year-old camel. The Prophet said: Give it to him, for the best of people are those who are best in repayment. (Narrated by Abu Dawud, Bab fi Husn al-Qada, p. 19, no. 3346) The lesson from this hadith is that if a buyer wants to give extra, he may do so. Footnote: The Prophet made a transaction for a young camel, then charity camels came to him, so he ordered me to repay the young camel. I found only a better camel, and he said to give that.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the book of sales: it is permissible (ja'iz) for the buyer to voluntarily increase the price paid to the seller. The author explains that this is an act of generosity from the buyer's own property. The proof is a hadith where the Prophet returned a superior camel for a borrowed one, indicating voluntary increase is praiseworthy. The commentary emphasizes that this is not obligatory but a virtuous act.

Key Terms
ثمن (thaman): Price; the consideration paid by the buyer in a sale.
مشترى (mushtari): Buyer; the person purchasing the commodity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a buyer voluntarily gives extra money to the seller after the sale is agreed?
A) It is not allowed because the price was fixed.
B) It is permissible but the seller must refuse.
C) It is permissible and recommended as a generous act.
D) It is required to maintain fairness.

Key Takeaway
A buyer may voluntarily increase the price for the seller as a praiseworthy act, supported by the Prophet's example of repaying a better camel.

Permissibility of Seller Increasing Commodity or Reducing Price
Permissibility for seller to give extra or reduce price

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a seller voluntarily increasing the commodity or reducing the price, and cite the hadith proof.

Core Idea
A seller may voluntarily give extra commodity or reduce the price; it is a commendable act.

This lesson examines a straightforward but important ruling: a seller's permission to voluntarily increase the sold item or decrease the price after the contract. Although such generosity is not obligatory, it is encouraged by the Sunnah. We will explore the legal basis from a hadith in Sunan Abi Dawud and understand the scope of this permission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text states that the seller is permitted (ja'iz) to increase the commodity (mabi') or reduce the price (thaman). Recognize that this is a voluntary act after the sale.
The ruling is mubah (permissible) with a recommendation.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Sunan Abi Dawud where the Prophet (saw) commanded a weigher to 'weigh and give extra' (zen wa arjih).
This hadith is ahad (single-narrator) but its chain is sound.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'give extra' indicates permissibility and encouragement. The Hanafi school derives permissibility from the general command, as it is not obligatory.
The command applies to any seller, not just weighers.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no significant ikhtilaf among the major schools on this basic permissibility; it is considered mustahabb (recommended).
All schools agree that voluntary concessions are allowed.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi position
The Hanafi position is based on the hadith and the principle that a person may dispose of his own property as he wishes, as long as it does not harm others.
The ruling also applies to giving a discount after the sale.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(١٤) ويجوز للبائع ان يزيد في المبيع ويجوز ان يحط من الثمن اور بائع کے لئے جائز ہے کہ مبیع میں زیادہ کر دے اور جائز ہے کہ شمن میں کمی کر دے۔ بائع کے لئے یہ بھی جائز ہے کہ جتنی مبیع طے ہوئی ہے اس سے زیادہ دے اور یہ بھی جائز ہے کہ جتنا من طے ہوا ہیں اس سے کم لے۔ اس کی ملکیت ہے وہ ایسا کر سکتا ہے (۲) مبیع زیادہ دینے کی ترغیب حدیث میں ہے۔ حدثنا سويد بن قيس ... ولم رجل يزن بالاجر فقال له رسول الله له زن و ارجح (ب) ( ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی الرجحان فی الوزن ص ۱۸ نمبر ۳۳۳۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بائع کو چاہئے کہ مبیع کو وزن میں کچھ زیادہ ہی دینا چاہئے۔ حاشیہ : (ب) وہاں ایک آدمی تھا جو اجرت پروزن کرتا تھا تو آپ نے فرمایا مجھکا کر تولا کرو۔
And it is permissible for the seller to increase in the commodity and it is permissible to reduce from the price. It is permissible for the seller to give more than the agreed commodity, and it is permissible to take less than the agreed price. It is his property, he may do so. (2) Encouragement to give extra commodity is in the hadith: Suwaid bin Qais narrated... a man was weighing with a wage, so the Messenger of Allah said: Weigh and make it abundant. (Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-Rajhan fi al-Wazn, p. 18, no. 3336) This hadith indicates that the seller should give a bit extra in weight. Footnote: There was a man who used to weigh for a wage, and the Prophet said: 'Weigh and give extra.'
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This ruling states that the seller is permitted to voluntarily increase the quantity of the sold commodity or reduce the price. Both actions are permissible as they come from the seller's own property. The author supports this with a hadith from Abu Dawud where the Prophet instructs a weigher to give extra weight, which is applied to sellers in general. This is a commendable act.

Key Terms
مبيع (mabi'): The commodity being sold.
يحط (yahuttu): To reduce or decrease the price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which action is permissible for the seller according to this ruling?
A) To increase the price after the sale.
B) To give extra commodity or reduce the price.
C) To cancel the sale unilaterally.
D) To demand immediate payment if not agreed.

Key Takeaway
A seller may voluntarily give extra goods or reduce the price; this is permissible and encouraged by the Sunnah.
