Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Entitlement After Price or Commodity Change
Inter-madhhab dispute on entitlement basis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on entitlement after voluntary increase/decrease, explain the Shafi'i counter-position, and apply the rule to murabaha and shuf'a cases.

Core Idea
Entitlement rights follow the final transaction, not the original agreement — a voluntary increase or decrease is integrated into the sale.

When a buyer voluntarily pays more than the agreed price, or a seller gives extra commodity or reduces the price, does this affect subsequent rights like murabaha and pre-emption? The Hanafi school says yes: all entitlement attaches to the final adjusted figures. The Shafi'i school disagrees, treating any later change as a separate gift. This lesson examines the disagreement and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core ruling: entitlement (istihqaq) for murabaha, tawliyah, and shuf'a attaches to the final price or commodity after any voluntary increase or decrease by either party.
The text gives examples: buyer pays 12 instead of 10; seller gives two items instead of one.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize Imam al-Shafi'i's position: entitlement attaches to the original agreed terms; any later change is a separate gift (hiba) and does not affect rights.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand Shafi'i's reasoning: the original contract is the basis; changes after the sale are new transactions, not modifications of the original.
The opponent's dalil is based on the principle that a sale is concluded on specific terms.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
See how the Hanafi school rebuts: the increase or decrease is done in the context of the same transaction and is assimilated into it, making the final figures the effective basis.
Hanafi uses a rational argument (dalil aqli): rights follow the actual exchange, not the initial agreement.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: in murabaha, Hanafi requires declaring the final cost; Shafi'i declares the original cost and treats the increase separately. For shuf'a, the pre-emption price differs accordingly.
The mufta bihi is the Hanafi view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۵) ويتعلق الاستحقاق بجميع ذلك اور استحقاق ان تمام کے ساتھ متعلق ہونگے۔ مثال: مشتری نے دس پونڈ قیمت کی تھی اس کے بجائے بارہ پونڈ دیئے تو اب مرابحہ اور تولیہ جو کرے گا وہ بارہ پونڈ پر کرے گا۔ اسی طرح بائع نے ایک مبیع کے بجائے دو بیع دس پونڈ میں دیدی تو اب یوں کہے گا کہ دو مبیع دس پونڈ میں لی ہیں۔ یوں نہیں کہے گا کہ ایک مبیع دس پونڈ میں لی ہے۔ اسی طرح بائع نے دس پونڈ کے بجائے آٹھ پونڈ لئے تو لینے والا یوں کہے گا کہ آٹھ پونڈ میں مبیع خریدی ہے۔ اور اسی آٹھ پونڈ پر مرابحہ اور تولیہ کرے گا۔ اب دس پونڈ پر مرابحہ یا تولیہ نہیں کرے گا۔ اسی طرح جو آدمی شفعہ کا دعوی کرے گا وہ اب موجودہ قیمت اور موجودہ بیع پر شفعہ کا دعوی کرے گا۔ کیونکہ اب یہی قیمت اصل بن گئی اور زیادہ دی ہوئی قیمت یا بائع کی جانب سے کم کی ہوئی قیمت ہی اصل بن گئی۔ اس لئے اب تمام حقوق اسی پر منحصر ہونگے۔ فاننده امام شافعی کی رائے یہ ہے کہ شروع میں جو قیمت یا مبیع طے ہوئی تھی وہی اصل ہے۔ اس کے ساتھ تمام حقوق متعلق ہوں گے۔ اور بعد میں جو مبیع زیادہ کی یا شمن زیادہ کئے وہ بعد کا ہدیہ اور ہبہ ہے اس کا تعلق اصل مبیع اور رشمن کے ساتھ نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے اس زیادتی کے ساتھ حقوق متعلق نہیں ہونگے۔
And entitlement attaches to all of that. Entitlement will be related to all of it. Example: The buyer had a price of ten pounds, but he gave twelve pounds instead; so when he does murabaha or tawliyah, he will do it on twelve pounds. Similarly, if the seller gave two commodities instead of one for ten pounds, then he will say: I bought two commodities for ten pounds. He will not say: I bought one commodity for ten pounds. Similarly, if the seller took eight pounds instead of ten, the buyer will say: I bought the commodity for eight pounds, and he will do murabaha and tawliyah on that eight pounds, not on ten pounds. Similarly, the person claiming shuf'a will claim on the current price and current sale. Because now this price has become the original, and the increased price or the decreased price from the seller has become the original. So all rights depend on it. The opinion of Imam Shafi'i is that the original price or commodity agreed at the beginning is the original. All rights attach to it. The later increase in commodity or price is a separate gift (hiba) and does not relate to the original sale, so rights do not attach to that increase.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage discusses the legal consequence when a buyer voluntarily increases the price or a seller gives extra commodity or reduces price. The Hanafi position is that entitlement rights (such as in murabaha, tawliyah, and shuf'a) attach to the final adjusted figures, not the original agreement. The author contrasts this with Imam Shafi'i's view, who considers the original terms as the basis and any later increase as a separate gift (hiba), thus not affecting the rights. The practical difference is seen in how resale on murabaha or claim of pre-emption is calculated.

Key Terms
استحقاق (istihqaq): Entitlement; the right that attaches based on the sale, such as the right to pre-emption (shuf'a) or profit calculation in murabaha.
شفعة (shuf'a): Right of pre-emption; a neighbour or partner's right to purchase property before others.
مرابحة (murabaha): A sale where the seller discloses the cost and adds a profit margin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a buyer voluntarily pays more than the agreed price, upon what amount is murabaha calculated?
A) The originally agreed price.
B) The final price after increase.
C) The average of the two prices.
D) The market value.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, any voluntary increase or decrease in price or commodity becomes the new basis for all entitlement rights in subsequent transactions.

Deferring an Immediate Price with a Known Term
Ruling on deferring immediate payment to a known future date

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on deferring an immediate payment and apply the condition that the term must be known.

Core Idea
A seller may defer an immediate payment to a known future date; the term must be known to be enforceable.

This passage addresses a common situation in sales: a seller initially asks for immediate payment but later agrees to postpone it. The Hanafi ruling clarifies that such a deferment is permissible and binding, provided the new payment date is clearly specified. The author supports this with a hadith showing the virtue of giving respite.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the seller deferring an originally immediate price to a future date. The ruling is that it becomes deferred (ja'iz, permissible).
The seller has the option to defer.
2
Locate the condition for validity
The deferment is valid only if the new term is known (ajal ma'loom). If unknown, it leads to dispute.
A known term prevents gharar (uncertainty).
3
Examine the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Bukhari about a man forgiven for ordering his workers to give respite and forgive the well-off. This shows the permissibility and virtue of deferring payment.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear (qat'i al-dalala).
4
Note the legal effect
Once deferred, the payment must be made on the specified date; it becomes binding.
The deferment is a unilateral change by the seller; the buyer's consent is implicit by acceptance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(١٦) ومن باع بثمن حال ثم اجله اجلا معلوما صار مؤجلا کسی نے فوری شمن کے ساتھ بچا پھر اس کو مؤخر کر دیا اجل معلوم کے ساتھ تو مو جل ہو جائے گا۔ کسی نے اس طرح بیع کی کہ ابھی قیمت دے گا لیکن بعد میں متعین تاریخ کے ساتھ مؤخر کر دیا تو اب مؤخر ہو جائے گا۔ اور متعین تاریخ پر قیمت دینی ہوگی۔ حدیث میں قیمت مؤخر کرنے کی ترغیب ہے ۔ ان حذیفة قال قال النبى الله تلقت الملائكة روح رجل ممن قبلكم فقالوا اعملت من الخير شيئا؟ قال كنت آمر فتیانی ان ينظروا ويتجاوزوا عن الموسر قال فتجاوزوا عنه (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب من انظر موسر اص ۲۷۹ نمبر ۷ ۲۰۷) اس حدیث میں پچھلے زمانے کے ایک آدمی کو اس بنا پر اللہ نے معاف کر دیا کہ وہ قیمت لینے میں مہلت دیا کرتا تھا۔ اس لئے قیمت لینے میں مہلت دینا جائز ہے۔ بشرطیکہ تاریخ معلوم ہو ورنہ جھگڑا ہو گا (۲) تاخیر دینا بائع کا اپنا اختیار ہے اس لئے وہ استعمال کر سکتا ہے۔
And whoever sells with an immediate price then defers it for a known term, it becomes deferred. If someone sells with immediate payment then later defers it for a known term, it becomes deferred. The price must be paid on the specified date. The hadith encourages deferring the price: Hudhaifa narrated that the Prophet said: The angels received the soul of a man from before you and asked: Did you do any good? He said: I used to order my young men to give respite and forgive the well-off. So they forgave him. (Bukhari, Bab man anzara mu'siran, p. 279, no. 7207) This hadith shows that giving respite in taking the price is permissible, provided the date is known, otherwise there would be dispute. (2) Deferring is the seller's own option, so he may exercise it.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This ruling states that if a seller originally sells for immediate payment (thaman hal), but later agrees to defer the payment to a known future date (ajal ma'loom), the payment becomes deferred and enforceable at that date. The author provides a hadith from Bukhari about a man who was forgiven for giving respite to debtors, indicating the virtue of deferment. However, the term must be known to avoid dispute. The seller has the right to defer at his discretion.

Key Terms
حال (haal): Immediate; payment due at the time of contract without delay.
مؤجل (mu'ajjal): Deferred; payment postponed to a future known date.
اجل معلوم (ajal ma'loom): Known term; the future date must be specified clearly to avoid uncertainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a seller sells with immediate payment but later agrees to defer the payment to a known future date?
A) The payment remains immediate and the deferment is invalid.
B) The payment becomes deferred and must be paid on that date.
C) The sale becomes void because the terms changed.
D) The buyer must pay immediately unless a new contract is made.

Key Takeaway
It is permissible for a seller to defer an immediate payment to a known future date, making it deferred and enforceable.

Deferment of Debts Except Loans
Rule on deferring immediate debts, except loans

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on deferment of immediate debts, identify the exception for loans, and explain the legal basis using the athar of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.

Core Idea
Deferring an immediate debt is binding, but a loan remains repayable on demand even if a term is set.

This passage extends the previous ruling on deferring the sale price to all immediate debts. The key rule is general: any dayn haal can be validly deferred by mutual agreement, making it payable only after the term. However, there is a critical exception: loans (qard) cannot be deferred; they remain immediate (hal) regardless of any agreed term. This distinction rests on the nature of the loan as a gratuitous act (tabarru'), where deferment would imply a time value akin to riba.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
Read the first part: 'every immediate debt, when its owner defers it, becomes deferred.' Grasp that this applies broadly to all debts that are due immediately (e.g., sale price, rent, etc.)
The rule makes deferment binding on the creditor.
2
Recognize the exception
The phrase 'except the loan (qard)' signals the only case where deferment is invalid. Note that this exception is absolute—even if both parties agree to a term, the loan remains payable on demand.
Contrast with the general rule: for a loan, setting a date does not defer the right to demand repayment.
3
Understand the rationale
The commentary explains: a loan is a gratuitous favor (ihsan) from the start. Deferring it would create a benefit (time value) for the lender, which is not allowed. Hence, the lender can demand repayment at any time.
This rationale prevents riba-like enrichment.
4
Analyze the proof (dalil)
The author cites the statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i: 'A loan is immediate (hal) even if it is to a term.' This athar is from the Musannaf of Ibn Abi Shayba. Understand that this is a zanni al-thubut (probable transmission) but qat'i al-dalala (clear meaning) for the Hanafi school.
The proof directly supports the exception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(١٧) وكل دين حال اذا اجله صاحبه صار مؤجلا الا القرض فان تأجيله لايصح ہر وہ دین جو فوری ہو اگر اس کو مؤخر کر دیا جائے تو موخر ہو جائے گا مگر قرض کہ اس کی تا خیر صحیح نہیں ہے۔ مثال: بیع کی قیمت مشتری پر فوری ہو اس کو مؤخر کر دیا تو وہ مؤخر ہو جائے گی۔ اب بائع تاریخ سے پہلے لینا چاہے تو نہیں لے سکے گا۔ تاخیر کرنے میں مبیع کی قیمت زیادہ ہو جاتی ہے اس لئے تاخیر کی بھی قیمت ہوئی اس لئے اس کو تاریخ سے پہلے نہیں لے سکتا۔ لیکن قرض تو شروع سے تبرع اور احسان ہے اس لئے جب چاہے قرض دینے والا واپس لے سکتا ہے۔ تاریخ متعین کرنے سے متعین نہیں ہوگی۔ قانونی طور پر پہلے بھی لے سکتا ہے۔ البتہ تاریخ پر لے تو بہتر ہے۔ اس اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن ابراهيم قال والقرض حال وان كان الى اجل (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبہ ۶۴ من قال القرض حال وان کان الی اجل، ج رابع ، ص ۳۲۴، نمبر ۲۰۵۷۸)
And every immediate debt, when its owner defers it, becomes deferred, except the loan (qard), for its deferment is invalid. Every debt that is immediate, if it is deferred, it becomes deferred, except a loan, because its deferment is not valid. Example: The price of a sale is immediate on the buyer; if the seller defers it, it becomes deferred. Now the seller cannot demand payment before the date. Because by deferring, the price gains a time value, so he cannot take before the date. But a loan is from the beginning a gratuitous act (tabarru') and favor (ihsan); therefore the lender can take it back whenever he wishes. Setting a date does not make it fixed. Legally, he can take it earlier. However, taking on the date is better. There is evidence for this: Ibrahim said: A loan is immediate (hal) even if it is to a term. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 64, man qala al-qard hal wa in kana ila ajal, vol. 4, p. 324, no. 20578)
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This ruling generalizes the previous rule: any immediate debt (such as a sale price) can be validly deferred to a future date by agreement. Once deferred, the creditor cannot demand payment before that date. The exception is a loan (qard), which by nature is a gratuitous contract; deferring a loan is not valid, meaning the lender retains the right to demand repayment at any time, even if a term was agreed. The author cites a statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that a loan is always considered immediate. This is because a loan is already an act of kindness, and adding a deferment would create a benefit (like time value) which is akin to riba, thus not allowed.

Key Terms
دين حال (dayn haal): An immediate debt, due at the time of contracting.
قرض (qard): A loan that is a gratuitous transfer of ownership with a promise of repayment; it is a benevolent transaction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is deferment of a loan (qard) invalid according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because a loan is a form of sale and deferment is not allowed in sales.
B) Because a loan is a gratuitous act and deferment would create a benefit akin to riba.
C) Because the borrower has the right to delay payment.
D) Because deferment of any debt is invalid in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, any immediate debt can be validly deferred except a loan, which remains immediately repayable even if a term is agreed, due to its gratuitous nature.

Deferring a Debt: Valid Except for Qard
Ruling on deferring immediate debts with proof and exception for qard

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on deferring an immediate debt, distinguish between a debt from a sale and a loan (qard), and apply the exception correctly.

Core Idea
You can defer any immediate debt except a loan — because qard is a benevolence that cannot be turned into a binding term.

In this passage, the author presents a foundational rule: any immediate debt, if the creditor defers it to a known term, becomes deferred and binding on the creditor. However, a loan (qard) is an exception. Understanding this distinction is crucial for contracts of sale and lending in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The text gives two sub-rulings: (a) deferring the price of a sale makes it deferred and binding; (b) deferring any immediate debt is valid except qard. Understand what each covers.
This is the core legal rule.
2
Examine the dalil from hadith
The hadith of Hudhayfah encourages giving respite to debtors. It indicates permissibility but not necessarily binding nature. The Hanafi school uses it to support the general validity of deferment.
The hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari.
3
Analyze the exception for qard
Why is qard different? Because it is inherently a gratuitous contract (tabarru'). The lender may demand repayment at any time regardless of a set term. Deferring qard is invalid.
This is supported by the statement of Ibrahim from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
4
Consider the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i views later additions to price or sold item as separate gifts, while Hanafi holds they attach to the original contract. Understand the practical difference.
This ikhtilaf affects rights and warranties.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذلک [۳۰] (١٦) ومن باع بثمن حال ثم اجله اجلا معلوما صار مؤجلا ۱۷۹۳۱) وكل دين حال اذا اجله صاحبه صار مؤجلا الا القرض فان تأجيله لايصح. اصول زیادہ دی ہوئی قیمت یا کم کی ہوئی قیمت یا زیادہ دی ہوئی صبیح اصل کے ساتھ لاحق ہو کر اب یہ اصل بن جائیگی (۲) اب تمام حقوق ان ہی کے ساتھ متعلق ہونگے ۔
فاننده امام شافعی کی رائے یہ ہے کہ شروع میں جو قیمت یا مبیع طے ہوئی تھی وہی اصل ہے۔ اس کے ساتھ تمام حقوق متعلق ہوں گے۔ اور بعد میں جو مبیع زیادہ کی یا شمن زیادہ کئے وہ بعد کا ہدیہ اور ہبہ ہے اس کا تعلق اصل مبیع اور رشمن کے ساتھ نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے اس زیادتی کے ساتھ حقوق متعلق نہیں ہونگے۔ (۱۹۳۰ (۱۶) کسی نے فوری شمن کے ساتھ بچا پھر اس کو مؤخر کر دیا اجل معلوم کے ساتھ تو مو جل ہو جائے گا۔ کسی نے اس طرح بیع کی کہ ابھی قیمت دے گا لیکن بعد میں متعین تاریخ کے ساتھ مؤخر کر دیا تو اب مؤخر ہو جائے گا۔ اور متعین تاریخ پر قیمت دینی ہوگی۔ حدیث میں قیمت مؤخر کرنے کی ترغیب ہے ۔ ان حذیفة قال قال النبى الله تلتقي الملائكة روح رجل ممن قبلكم فقالوا اعملت من الخير شيئا؟ قال كنت آمر فتیانی ان ينظروا ويتجاوزوا عن الموسر قال فتجاوزوا عنه (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب من انظر موسر اص ۲۷۹ نمبر ۷ ۲۰۷) اس حدیث میں پچھلے زمانے کے ایک آدمی کو اس بنا پر اللہ نے معاف کر دیا کہ وہ قیمت لینے میں مہلت دیا کرتا تھا۔ اس لئے قیمت لینے میں مہلت دینا جائز ہے۔ بشرطیکہ تاریخ معلوم ہو ورنہ جھگڑا ہو گا (۲) تاخیر دینا بائع کا اپنا اختیار ہے اس لئے وہ استعمال کر سکتا ہے۔ ت حال : ابھی فوری۔ اجلا : تاخیر کے ساتھ۔
[۱۹۳۱ (۱۷) ہر وہ دین جو فوری ہو اگر اس کو مؤخر کر دیا جائے تو موخر ہو جائے گا مگر قرض کہ اس کی تا خیر صحیح نہیں ہے۔
ت مثلا بیع کی قیمت مشتری پر فوری ہو اس کو مؤخر کر دیا تو وہ مؤخر ہو جائے گی۔ اب بائع تاریخ سے پہلے لینا چاہے تو نہیں لے سکے گا۔ تاخیر کرنے میں مبیع کی قیمت زیادہ ہو جاتی ہے اس لئے تاخیر کی بھی قیمت ہوئی اس لئے اس کو تاریخ سے پہلے نہیں لے سکتا۔ لیکن قرض تو شروع سے تبرع اور احسان ہے اس لئے جب چاہے قرض دینے والا واپس لے سکتا ہے۔ تاریخ متعین کرنے سے متعین نہیں ہوگی۔ قانونی طور پر پہلے بھی لے سکتا ہے۔ البتہ تاریخ پر لے تو بہتر ہے۔ اس اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن ابراهيم قال والقرض حال وان كان الى اجل (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبہ ۶۴ من قال القرض حال وان کان الی اجل، ج رابع ، ص ۳۲۴، نمبر ۲۰۵۷۸)
حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا تم سے پہلی قوم میں ایک آدمی کی روح فرشتہ نے قبضہ کرنا چاہا تو انہوں نے کہا تم نے کوئی خیر کا کام کیا ہے ؟ اس آدمی نے کہا کہ میں نوجوان کو حکم دیتا تھا کہ تنگدستوں کو مہلت دیں اور درگذر کریں۔ حضور نے فرمایا تو اللہ نے ان کو معاف کر دیا (ب) قرض فوری ہوتا ہے چاہے مؤخر کر کے لینے کا وعدہ ہو۔
That [30] (16) Whoever sells with an immediate price then defers it with a known term, it becomes deferred. (1931) And every immediate debt, when its owner defers it, becomes deferred, except a loan (qard), for its deferment is not valid. Principles: The additional given price or reduced price or additional given thing attaches to the original and becomes part of it. (2) All rights now pertain to it. Then Imam Shafi'i's opinion is that the original price or sold item agreed upon at the beginning is the basis; all rights pertain to it. Any later addition to the sold item or price is a subsequent gift (hiba) and has no relation to the original sold item and price, so rights do not attach to that addition. (1930) (16) Someone sold with an immediate price then deferred it with a known term, it becomes deferred. If someone sold such that the price is to be paid immediately but later defers it with a specified date, it becomes deferred and the price is due on that date. The hadith encourages deferring the price: Hudhayfah reported that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The angels met the soul of a man from those before you and asked: Did you do any good deed? He said: I used to order my servants to give respite and be lenient with the wealthy. So they pardoned him.' (Bukhari, Bab Man Anzara Mu'siran, no. 207). This hadith shows that a man from a previous nation was forgiven by Allah because he used to give respite in taking payment. Therefore, giving respite in taking payment is permissible provided the term is known, otherwise there will be dispute. (2) Giving respite is the seller's own choice, so he can exercise it. t=hal: immediate; ajala: with delay. (1931) (17) Every debt that is immediate, if it is deferred, becomes deferred, except a loan (qard), for its deferment is not valid. For example, the price of a sale is immediate on the buyer; if he defers it, it becomes deferred. Now the seller cannot take it before the date because the deferment increases the value of the sold item, so the deferment has a price; thus he cannot take it before the date. But a loan is from the beginning a donation and favor, so the lender can take it back whenever he wishes; it is not fixed by setting a term. Legally, he can take it earlier, but it is better to take at the term. There is evidence for this: Ibrahim said, 'A loan is immediate even if it is to a term.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 64 Man Qala al-Qard Hal wa In Kana ila Ajalin, vol. 4, p. 324, no. 20578). Footnote: (a) He said: 'A man from the previous nations, the angels took his soul and asked: Did you do any good? He said: I used to order my young men to give respite to the destitute and forgive them. The Prophet said: So Allah forgave him.' (b) A loan is immediate even if there is a promise to defer.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The text presents two related rulings: (1) If a seller sells with an immediate price and then later defers it for a known term, the price becomes deferred (mujjal). (2) Any immediate debt, if the creditor defers it, becomes deferred except for a loan (qard). The Hanafi school holds that deferring an immediate debt is valid and binding on the creditor; he cannot demand payment before the term. The exception for qard is because a loan is inherently a transaction of benevolence (tabarru') and does not involve a contract for deferment. The text cites a hadith encouraging giving respite to debtors and also quotes Ibrahim's statement that a loan remains immediate even if a term is set. This distinction is crucial in Hanafi fiqh: deferring a debt arising from a sale creates a new obligation enforceable at the term, whereas deferring a qard is ineffective because it contradicts the nature of qard as a gratuitous contract. The commentary also explains that the default rule is immediate payment; deferment is an exception that requires the creditor's consent and a known term.

Key Terms
دين حال (dayn hal): An immediate debt that is due without delay.
تأجيل (ta'jil): Postponing the due date of a debt to a future known term.
قرض (qard): A loan given as a benevolence (qard hasan) with the expectation of repayment without increase.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following is true about deferring a loan (qard)?
A) It becomes deferred if a term is set.
B) It remains immediate and the lender can demand repayment at any time.
C) It is only valid if the term is more than one year.
D) It becomes a sale.

Key Takeaway
Deferring a debt from a sale is valid and binding on the creditor, but deferring a qard is invalid because a loan is a pure benevolence that cannot be turned into a binding term.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

The Prohibition of Riba and Its Hanafi Causes
Ruling with proof: prohibition of riba and derivation of its causes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of riba, cite the primary textual evidence (Quran 2:275 and the Hadith of the six commodities), and identify the two causes (illa) of riba according to the Hanafi school: measurement (kayl) or weight (wazn) combined with same genus (jins).

Core Idea
Riba is haram in every makil or mawzun item sold with the same genus; the cause is kayl or wazn with same jins.

This passage introduces the chapter on riba in the book of sales. It establishes the definitive prohibition from the Quran and the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, then defines the specific conditions under which an excess or deferment becomes unlawful. Understanding the causes (illa) – measurement (kayl) or weight (wazn) combined with sameness of genus – is the key to determining when an exchange crosses into riba. The Hanafi school derives these causes from the six commodities mentioned in the hadith, and they govern all subsequent applications.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the act and its ruling
The act is any sale or exchange involving riba. The ruling is haram (prohibited). First, note the definition: any excess without consideration in a transaction.
The prohibition is absolute but only applies under specific conditions (illa).
2
2. Locate the dalil (proof)
The text cites two primary proofs: the Quranic verse (2:275) '...and Allah has permitted trade and prohibited usury', and the hadith of the six commodities (gold, silver, wheat, barley, dates, salt) where the Prophet ﷺ said 'like for like, hand to hand' and warned against excess.
The Quran gives the general prohibition; the hadith details the specific categories and conditions.
3
3. Trace the wajh al-dalalah from the hadith
From the hadith, the Hanafi school extracts that the prohibition applies when two conditions are met: (a) the items are of the same genus (jins), and (b) they are customarily measured (makil) or weighed (mawzun). The phrase 'like for like' indicates equality, and 'hand to hand' indicates spot delivery.
The six commodities are not exhaustive; they serve as examples from which the common cause (illa) is derived.
4
4. Identify the causes (illa) from the school's derivation
The Hanafi ʿilla for riba is twofold: (a) measurement (kayl) combined with same genus, and (b) weight (wazn) combined with same genus. If either of these combinations exists, any excess (riba al-fadl) or deferment (riba al-nasiʾah) is prohibited.
Items outside these categories (e.g., counted items, length-measured items) are not subject to riba rules in the Hanafi school.
5
5. Apply the rule to examples
Use the causes to test exchanges: e.g., wheat (makil) for wheat (same jins) must be equal and spot. Wheat for rice (different jins) allows excess. Gold (mawzun) for gold must be equal and spot; gold for silver (different jins) permits excess.
The modern practice of weighing grains does not change the category; the ruling is based on the customary method at the time of the Prophet.

Chapter of Riba [932] (1) Riba is prohibited in every measured (makil) or weighed (mawzun) item when sold with its genus with excess. [933] (2) Chapter of Riba. Necessary note: Any excess that is without consideration is called riba. Here, specific excess is called riba and usury, which is prohibited. The evidence for its prohibition is the verse: 'Allah has permitted trade and prohibited usury' (Quran 2:275). And its principle is in the hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Gold for gold, silver for silver, wheat for wheat, barley for barley, dates for dates, salt for salt, like for like, hand to hand. Whoever gives more or asks for more has committed riba. The taker and the giver are equal in sin.' (Muslim, Bab al-Sarf wa Bay' al-Dhahab bi al-Wariq; Bukhari, Bab Bay' al-Fidda bi al-Fidda; Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-Sarf; Tirmidhi, Bab Ma Ja'a an al-Hintah bi al-Hintha Mithlan bi Mithl wa Karahiyat al-Tafadul). These hadiths establish that selling an item of the same genus, if it is measured or weighed, with excess is prohibited. [932] (1) Riba is prohibited in measured or weighed items when sold with the same genus with excess. Measured items are those that in previous times were measured by volume (kayl) and sa'; like wheat, rice, and grains. Weighed items are those weighed on scales; like dirhams, dinars, and iron. So if it is a measured item and the sold good (mabī') and price (thaman) are of the same genus, e.g., both sides are wheat, taking wheat for wheat, or rice for rice, or dirhams for dirhams, or dinars for dinars, then because both sides are the same type, it must be equal; excess would be riba and prohibited. And it must be hand to hand (spot). If either is deferred, it becomes riba. The reason is the hadith above. Bi jinsih: both sides are the same type; e.g., the sold good is wheat and the price is also wheat. (933) (2) So the cause (illa) of riba is measurement (kayl) along with genus, and weight (wazn) along with genus. For riba there are two causes: (1) Both sides are the same genus, then excess is prohibited. If one side is wheat and the other is rice, excess is permissible; one can take one kilo of wheat for two kilos of rice. (2) The second cause is that the item is measured by volume (kayl) like all grains that in previous times were measured by volume; nowadays they are weighed on scales; or it is weighed like dirhams and dinars. So if an item is neither measured by volume nor weighed, e.g., counted items or measured by length (like cloth hand spans), then one handspan of cloth... Footnote: (a) He said: (1) Gold for gold, (2) silver for silver, (3) wheat for wheat, (4) barley for barley, (5) dates for dates, (6) salt for salt, like for like, hand to hand. Whoever gives more or asks for more has committed riba, the taker and the giver are equal in sin.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage begins the chapter on Riba in the book of sales. It defines riba as any excess without consideration and states its prohibition from the Quran (2:275) and the famous hadith of the six commodities. The Hanafi school identifies the cause (illa) of riba as measurement (kayl) or weight (wazn) combined with same genus (jins). This means that riba only applies to items that are customarily sold by volume or weight when exchanged with items of the same type. For example, selling wheat for wheat requires equality in measure and spot delivery; any excess or deferment makes it riba. If the genera differ (wheat for rice), excess is permissible. Items that are counted (like eggs) or measured by length (like cloth) are not subject to riba according to the Hanafi view. The passage also clarifies that the prohibition covers both increase (fadl) and deferment (nasi'ah). The hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri is the primary textual evidence, and the Hanafi school uses it to derive the causes.

Key Terms
ربوا (riba): An excess without consideration in a transaction; specifically, usury or interest.
مكيل (makil): An item sold by volume measurement (kayl), such as grains.
موزون (mawzun): An item sold by weight (wazn), such as gold, silver, iron.
جنس (jins): Genus or type; in riba, items of the same jins trigger the requirement of equality and spot delivery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what are the two causes (illa) for riba?
A) Weight and genus together; measurement and genus together
B) Hand-to-hand delivery and equality
C) Genus and deferment
D) Volume and numerical count

Key Takeaway
Riba is haram only when both same genus and the item is makil or mawzun; excess or deferment in such cases is unlawful.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate

The Hanafi Cause of Riba: Measurement/Weight with Same Genus
Defines riba, cites evidence, explains cause, contrasts with Shafi'i view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi 'illah for riba in commodity exchanges and contrast it with the Shafi'i 'illah, identifying the textual basis and practical consequence.

Core Idea
Riba in commodities is triggered by measurement/weight plus same genus – not by food or price alone.

This passage introduces the Hanafi position on the prohibition of riba (usury/interest) in sales. While riba is widely known in money-lending, this text focuses on commodity exchanges – the hidden pitfalls of trading measured or weighed items of the same kind. We'll see how the Hanafi school derives the effective cause ('illah) from the famous hadith of six commodities and why the Shafi'i school reaches a different conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited act and its evidence
Recognise that the passage forbids riba in measured or weighed items sold with their own genus with disparity. Note the primary dalil: Quran 2:275 and the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri listing six commodities.
The hadith is the key text from which both schools derive their 'illah.
2
Extract the Hanafi 'illah
The Hanafi school identifies the common trait among the six items: gold and silver are weighed, wheat, barley, dates and salt are measured. Thus, the 'illah is kail (measurement) or wazn (weight) combined with same genus (jins). Riba occurs only in items that are customarily measured or weighed.
Items sold by count or length are excluded because no hadith specifies them.
3
Compare with the Shafi'i 'illah
The Shafi'i school reads the same hadith and concludes that gold and silver are prices (thamaniyyah) and the other four are food (ta'am). Their 'illah is jins + thamaniyyah or jins + ta'am. Note their dalil: the Daraqutni hadith adding 'eaten or drunk'.
The Hanafi response argues that if thamaniyyah were the cause, wheat and salt should not be included. The Daraqutni hadith is mursal and thus weaker.
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Under Hanafi law, iron and lime are ribawi (weighed), so they cannot be exchanged unequally. Under Shafi'i law, they are not ribawi because they are neither thaman nor food, so unequal exchange is permissible.
This difference affects modern commodities like steel, cement, etc.

Source Text

باب الربوا م

ضروری نوٹ ایسی زیادتی جو عوض سے خالی ہو اس کو ربوا کہتے ہیں۔ یہاں مخصوص زیادتی کو ر ہوا اور سود کہا ہے جو حرام ہے۔ اس کے حرام ہونے کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے و احل الله البيع وحرم الربوا ( آیت ۲۷۵ سورة البقرة ۲) اس آیت میں سود کو حرام کہا گیا ہے۔ اور اس کا اصول اس حدیث میں ہے عن ابی سعید الخدری قال قال رسول الله الله الله الذهب بالذهب والفضة بالفضة والبر بالبر والشعير بالشعير والتمر بالتمر والملح بالملح مثلا بمثل يدا بيد فمن زاد او استزاد فقد اربي الآخذ والمعطى فيه مسواء (الف) ( مسلم شریف ، باب الصرف وبيع الذهب بالورق ص ۲۴ نمبر ۴۰۶۴/۱۵۸۷ / بخاری شریف، باب بیج الفضة بالفضة ص۲۹۰ نمبر ۲۱۷۰/۲۱۷۶ را بود او د شریف ، باب فی الصرف ص ۱۱۹ نمبر ۳۳۴۹ / ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء ان المحطة بالحطة مثلا بمثل وكراهية التفاضل فید ص ۲۳۵ نمبر ۱۲۴۰) ان احادیث میں ایک جنس کی چیز ہو اور کیلی یا وزنی ہو تو کمی بیشی کر کے بیچنا حرام قرار دیا ہے۔

[۹۳۲] (۱) ربوا حرام ہے کیلی یا وزنی چیز میں جبکہ بیچا جائے اسی جنس سے کمی بیشی کر کے۔ ر کیلی چیز وہ ہے جو پچھلے زمانے میں کیلی اور صاع میں رکھ کر بیچتے تھے۔ جیسے گیہوں، چاول اور غلہ وغیرہ۔ اور وزنی جو تر از و سے وزن کیا جاتا ہے جیسے درہم اور دنا نیر اور لوہا وغیرہ۔ پس کیلی چیز ہو اور مبیع اور ثمن ایک جنس کے ہوں مثلا دونوں طرف گیہوں ہو کہ گیہوں کے بدلے گیہوں لے رہا ہو یا چاول کے بدلے چاول لے رہا ہو یا درہم کے بدلے درہم لے رہا ہو یا دینار کے بدلے دینار لے رہا ہو تو چونکہ ان بیوع میں دونوں طرف ایک ہی قسم کی چیز ہے اس لئے برابر سرا بر لینا ہوگا۔ کمی بیشی کرے گا تو سود ہوگا اور حرام ہوگا ۔ اور نقد قبضہ کرنا ہوگا ۔ دونوں میں سے ایک بھی ادھار ہوگا تو سود ہو جائے گا۔ حرام ہونے کی وجہ اوپر کی حدیث ہے۔

بجنہ : ایک ہی قسم کی چیز دونوں طرف ہوں ، مثلا طبیع میں بھی گیہوں اور شمن بھی گیہوں ہو۔

(۹۳۳) (۲) پس علت ربوا میں کیل ہے جنس کے ساتھ اور وزن ہے جنس کے ساتھ۔ ربوا ہونے کے لئے دو علتیں ہیں (۱) دونوں طرف ایک ہی قسم کی چیز ہوتب کمی بیشی حرام ہے پس اگر ایک طرف گیہوں ہو اور دوسری طرف چاول ہو تو کمی بیشی جائز ہے۔ ایک کیلو گیہوں دیگر دو کیلو چاول لے سکتا ہے (۲) اور دوسری علت یہ ہے کہ وہ چیز کیل سے ناپی جاتی ہو جیسے تمام غلے کہ پچھلے زمانے میں ان کو کیل سے ناپتے تھے۔ اس زمانے میں ان کو تر از و سے وزن کرتے ہیں ۔ یا وزن کئے جاتے ہوں جیسے در ہم اور دنا نیر ۔ پس اگر ایسی چیز ہو جو نہ کیل کی جاتی ہے اور نہ وزن کی جاتی ہو مثلا عددی ہو یا رائی ہو کہ ہاتھ سے ناپی جاتی ہو تو ایک ہاتھ کپڑا

حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا (۱) سونا سونے کے بدلے میں (۲) چاندی چاندی کے بدلے میں (۳) گیہوں گیہوں کے بدلے میں (۴) جو جو کے بدلے میں (۵) کھجور کھجور کے بدلے میں (۶) اور نمک نمک کے بدلے برابر سرابر ، ہاتھوں ہاتھ ، ہپس جس نے زیادہ دیایا زیادہ مانگا تو تو سود لینے والا اور دینے والا گناہ میں برابر

فالعلة فيه الكيل مع الجنس والوزن مع الجنس [۹۳۴] (۳) فاذا بيع المكيل بجنسه او الموزون بجنسه مثلا بمثل جاز البيع وان تفاضلا لم يجز.

دے کر دو ہاتھ کپڑا لے سکتا ہے۔ یا ایک اخروٹ دے کر دو اخروٹ لے سکتا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ احادیث میں عددی یا ذراعی کے ربوا کے سلسلے میں کچھ وارد نہیں ہوا ہے۔ اوپر جو ابوسعید خدری کی حدیث گزری اس میں درہم ودنا نیر کا ذکر ہے جو وزنی ہیں اور گیہوں ، جو کھجور اور نمک کو برابر سرا بر لینے کا تذکرہ ہے جو کیلی ہیں۔ اس لئے حفیہ کے نزدیک چیز یا وزنی ہو یا کیل ہو تب سود ہوگا۔ (1) وزن کو علت بنانے کی وجہ اس حدیث کا اشارہ بھی ہے۔ عن فضالة بن عبيد قال كنا مع رسول الله يوم خيبر نبايع اليهود الأوقية الذهب بالدينارين والثلاثة فقال رسول الله لا تبيعوا الذهب بالذهب الا وزنا بوزن (الف)(مسلم شریف ، باب بیع القلادة فيها خرز وذهب ص ۲۵ نمبر ۱۵۹۱ بر ۴۰۷۸) اس حدیث میں ہے وزنا بوزن، اس سے بھی اس علت کا اشارہ ملتا ہے کہ چیز وزنی ہوتب سود ہوگا (۲) دار قطنی کی حدیث میں وزنی اور کیلی چیزیں سود ہونے کی صراحت ہے۔عن سعید بن المسيب ان رسول الله لا قال لا ربوا الا فى ذهب أو فضة او مما يكال او يوزن ويؤكل ويشرب (ب) (دار قطنی، كتاب البيوع، ج

امام شافعی کے نزدیک سود کی علت کیلی اور وزنی نہیں ہے بلکہ ایک جنس ہو اور ثمنیت ہو یا کھانے کی چیڑ ہو تو اس میں ربوا ہو گا۔ دوہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ضروری نوٹ میں حضرت ابو سعید خدری کی حدیث میں سونا اور چاندی ہیں جن میں منیت ہے یعنی شن اور قیمت بننے کی صلاحیت ہے۔ اور گیہوں ، جو ، کھجور اور نمک کھانے کی چیزیں ہیں اس لئے منیت اور کھانا سود کی علت ہوگی (۲) دار قطنی کی حدیث جو اوپر گزری اس میں سونا اور چاندی کے ساتھ یوکل و یشرب کی تصریح ہے جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ کھانا سود کی علت ہے۔ اس لئے ان کے یہاں طبیع اور شمن ایک ہی چیز ہوں اور وہ چیز یا شمن میں سے ہو یا کھانے میں سے ہو تب سود ہوگا۔ اس لئے چونا اور لو ہے مین ان کے یہاں سود نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ نہ ثمن ہیں اور نہ کھائے جاتے ہیں۔

اصول سود کی علت (۱) جنس ایک ہو (۲) اور شمن بنے کی یا کھانے کی چیز ہو۔ ۹۳۴] (۳) پس اگر کیلی چیز اس کے جنس کے ساتھ بیچی جائے، یا وزنی چیز اس کے جنس کے ساتھ بیچی جائے برابر سرا بر تو بیع جائز ہے اور اگر کمی بیشی کرے تو جائز نہیں ہے۔ طبع اوشن دونوں ایک قسم کی چیزیں ہوں مثلا دونوں طرف گیہوں ہوں یا دونوں طرف وزنی چیز سونا ہوں تو دونوں کو برابر سرا بر نیچے تو جائز ہے اور کمی بیشی سے بیچے تو جائز نہیں ہے۔ حدیث گزر چکی ہے۔ عن ابی سعید الخدري قال قال رسول الله الله الذهب بالذهب والفضة بالفضة والبر بالبر والشعير بالشعير والتمر بالتمر والملح بالملح مثلا بمثل يدا بيد فمن زاد او حاشیہ : (الف) ہم حضور کے ساتھ خیبر میں تھے، یہود کے ساتھ بیچ کرتے تھے سونے کو دو دینار اور تین دینار کے بدلے تو حضور نے فرما یا مت بیچ سونے کو سونے کے بدلے مگر برابر سرابر وزن کر کے (ب) آپ نے فرمایا نہیں رہوا ہے مگر سونے میں اور چاندی میں یا جو کیل کیا جاتا ہو یا وزن کیا جاتا ہے یا کھایا جاتا ہو یا پیا جاتا ہو۔
Chapter of Riba. Book of Sales. [932] (1) Riba is prohibited in every measured (kaili) or weighed (mawzun) item when sold with its genus with excess. [933] (2)... Necessary note: Such an increase that is devoid of compensation is called riba. Here, specific increase is called riba and usury, which is forbidden. The evidence for its prohibition is the verse: 'And Allah has permitted trade and forbidden riba' (2:275). This verse declares riba forbidden. And its principle is in this hadith: From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Gold for gold, silver for silver, wheat for wheat, barley for barley, dates for dates, salt for salt, like for like, hand to hand; whoever increases or asks for increase has committed riba—the taker and the giver are equal therein.' (Muslim, Bukhari, Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi). In these hadiths, if an item is of one genus and is measured or weighed, selling it with excess is declared forbidden. [932] (1) Riba is forbidden in a measured or weighed item when sold with its genus with excess. A measured item is what was previously sold by measure and sa', like wheat, rice, grains, etc. A weighed item is what is weighed with a scale, like dirhams, dinars, iron, etc. So if the item is measured and the sold commodity (mabi') and price (thaman) are of the same genus—e.g., wheat for wheat, rice for rice, dirhams for dirhams, dinars for dinars—then because both sides are the same type, it must be equal. If one exceeds, it becomes riba and is forbidden. Also, immediate possession is required; if either is deferred, riba occurs. The reason for prohibition is the above hadith. [933] (2) So the cause ('illah) of riba is measurement (kail) with genus, and weight (wazn) with genus. There are two causes for riba: (1) Both sides are the same type—then excess is forbidden. If one side is wheat and the other rice, excess is permissible; one kg wheat can be exchanged for two kg rice. (2) The item is measured by kail, like all grains that were measured in the past (now weighed), or weighed, like dirhams and dinars. So if an item is neither measured nor weighed—e.g., counted or measured by the cubit (dhira')—then one cubit of cloth can be given for two cubits, or one walnut for two walnuts, because no hadith about riba has come regarding counted or cubit-measured items. The above hadith of Abu Sa'id mentions dirhams and dinars (weighed) and wheat, barley, dates, salt (measured). Thus, according to the Hanafis, only items that are weighed or measured incur riba. (1) The evidence for weight as a cause is the hadith of Fadala ibn 'Ubayd: We were with the Messenger of Allah at Khaybar, selling gold for two or three dinars, and he said: 'Do not sell gold for gold except weight for weight.' This hadith indicates that weight is a cause. (2) Al-Daraqutni's hadith states: 'There is no riba except in gold, silver, or what is measured or weighed and is eaten or drunk.' This mursal hadith explicitly states that gold, silver, and measured/weighed items that are eaten and drunk are subject to riba. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, the cause of riba is not kail and wazn, but rather same genus and thamaniyyah (being a price) or being food. He argues that in the hadith of Abu Sa'id, gold and silver have thamaniyyah (ability to be price), and wheat, barley, dates, salt are food, so thamaniyyah and food are the causes. (2) The hadith of al-Daraqutni specifies 'eaten or drunk' with gold and silver, meaning food is the cause. Thus, according to Shafi'i, if the mabi' and thaman are the same thing and that thing is either thaman (price) or food, then riba applies. So lime and iron are not subject to riba for him because they are neither thaman nor eaten. The principle of riba's cause: (1) same genus (2) and being thaman or food. [934] (3) So if a measured item is sold with its genus, or a weighed item with its genus, equal for equal, the sale is valid; if they are unequal, it is not valid. Both items must be of the same type, e.g., wheat for wheat, or weighed item like gold for gold—they must be equal; if sold with excess, it is not valid. The hadith has passed: From Abu Sa'id...
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on riba (usury/interest) in the context of sales. The author begins by defining riba as an increase devoid of compensation and declares it prohibited in all measured (kaili) or weighed (mawzun) items when sold with their own genus with disparity. The primary evidence is Quran 2:275, which permits trade but forbids riba, and the famous hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri listing six commodities (gold, silver, wheat, barley, dates, salt) that must be exchanged like-for-like and hand-to-hand. The Hanafi position is that the effective cause ('illah) for riba is measurement or weight combined with same genus. Thus, riba occurs only in items that are customarily measured by volume (like grains) or by weight (like precious metals). Items sold by count or length (like cloth or nuts) are not subject to riba-based prohibition, as no hadith specifies them. The passage then contrasts the Shafi'i view, which holds that the cause is thamaniyyah (being a price, as in gold/silver) or being food (as in the other four commodities). The Shafi'i school uses the same hadith but derives a different 'illah, also citing the Daraqutni hadith that adds 'eaten or drunk'. The Hanafis respond by pointing out that the three additional commodities (wheat, barley, salt) are not typically used as currency, so thamaniyyah cannot be the sole cause; rather, the common element is that they are all measured or weighed. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that under Hanafi law, items like iron and lime are ribawi because they are weighed, whereas Shafi'is exempt them since they are neither thaman nor food.

Key Terms
الربوا (al-ribā): An increase devoid of compensation in a transaction of same-genus items that are measured or weighed.
مكيل (makīl): An item customarily sold by volume measure (like grains).
موزون (mawzūn): An item customarily sold by weight (like gold, silver, iron).
جنس (jins): The genus or type of the commodity; same genus means the two items are fundamentally the same substance (e.g., wheat for wheat).
علة ('illah): The effective legal cause that triggers the ruling of riba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the effective cause ('illah) for riba in commodity exchanges?
A) Thamaniyyah and being food
B) Being measured or weighed combined with same genus
C) Being edible and drinkable
D) Being gold or silver only

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school identifies the 'illah of riba as measurement or weight combined with same genus, extending riba prohibition to all such commodities.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
The Effective Cause of Riba: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on the 'illa of riba with hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to contrast the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the 'illa of riba, identify the key hadith evidence for each, and apply the Hanafi 'illa to determine whether a given item is ribawi.

Core Idea
Riba applies to all weighed or measured items of the same genus, not just food or money.

The prohibition of riba is clear, but what makes an item ribawi? This lesson explores a major inter-madhhab dispute: the effective cause ('illa) of riba. The Hanafi school holds that the 'illa is weight (wazn) or measure (kayl) combined with genus identity, while the Shafi'i school limits it to food and monetary value. We will examine the hadith evidence each side uses and see how this difference plays out in practice.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on the 'illa
Identify the precise 'illa: weight or measure plus sameness of genus. Note that counted or arm-length items are excluded.
2
Identify the Hanafi dalil
Locate the hadith evidence: the hadith of Fadala ibn Ubaid emphasizing 'weight for weight' and the hadith of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab explicitly mentioning weighed and measured items.
These ahadith are the core of the Hanafi proof.
3
State the Shafi'i position and their dalil
Shafi'i holds the 'illa is thamaniyyah (for gold/silver) and food (for the other four items). Their evidence: the six items in Abu Sa'id's hadith are clearly either thaman or food; the Dar Qutni hadith says 'eaten and drunk'.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school argues that the explicit mention of weight and measure in the hadiths cannot be ignored; the Shafi'i reading discards the common factor of weight/measure.
This is the point of contention in istidlal.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Hanafi, copper and iron are ribawi if sold by weight; under Shafi'i, they are not. Also, counted items like walnuts are not ribawi in either school.

(3) فاذا بيع المكيل بجنسه او الموزون بجنسه مثلا بمثل جاز البيع وان تفاضلا لم يجز.

دے کر دو ہاتھ کپڑا لے سکتا ہے۔ یا ایک اخروٹ دے کر دو اخروٹ لے سکتا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ احادیث میں عددی یا ذراعی کے ربوا کے سلسلے میں کچھ وارد نہیں ہوا ہے۔ اوپر جو ابوسعید خدری کی حدیث گزری اس میں درہم ودنا نیر کا ذکر ہے جو وزنی ہیں اور گیہوں ، جو کھجور اور نمک کو برابر سرا بر لینے کا تذکرہ ہے جو کیلی ہیں۔ اس لئے حفیہ کے نزدیک چیز یا وزنی ہو یا کیل ہو تب سود ہوگا۔ (1) وزن کو علت بنانے کی وجہ اس حدیث کا اشارہ بھی ہے۔ عن فضالة بن عبيد قال كنا مع رسول الله يوم خيبر نبايع اليهود الأوقية الذهب بالدينارين والثلاثة فقال رسول الله لا تبيعوا الذهب بالذهب الا وزنا بوزن (الف)(مسلم شریف ، باب بیع القلادة فيها خرز وذهب ص ۲۵ نمبر ۱۵۹۱ بر ۴۰۷۸) اس حدیث میں ہے وزنا بوزن، اس سے بھی اس علت کا اشارہ ملتا ہے کہ چیز وزنی ہوتب سود ہوگا (۲) دار قطنی کی حدیث میں وزنی اور کیلی چیزیں سود ہونے کی صراحت ہے۔عن سعید بن المسيب ان رسول الله لا قال لا ربوا الا فى ذهب أو فضة او مما يكال او يوزن ويؤكل ويشرب (ب) (دار قطنی، كتاب البيوع، ج ثالث ص ا ا نمبر ۲۸۱۰) اس حدیث مرسل میں صراحت ہے کہ سونا، چاندی یا کیلی اور وزنی چیزیں سود ہیں جو کھائی اور پی جاتی ہوں۔

امام شافعی کے نزدیک سود کی علت کیلی اور وزنی نہیں ہے بلکہ ایک جنس ہو اور ثمنیت ہو یا کھانے کی چیڑ ہو تو اس میں ربوا ہو گا۔ دوہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ضروری نوٹ میں حضرت ابو سعید خدری کی حدیث میں سونا اور چاندی ہیں جن میں منیت ہے یعنی شن اور قیمت بننے کی صلاحیت ہے۔ اور گیہوں ، جو ، کھجور اور نمک کھانے کی چیزیں ہیں اس لئے منیت اور کھانا سود کی علت ہوگی (۲) دار قطنی کی حدیث جو اوپر گزری اس میں سونا اور چاندی کے ساتھ یوکل و یشرب کی تصریح ہے جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ کھانا سود کی علت ہے۔ اس لئے ان کے یہاں طبیع اور شمن ایک ہی چیز ہوں اور وہ چیز یا شمن میں سے ہو یا کھانے میں سے ہو تب سود ہوگا۔ اس لئے چونا اور لو ہے مین ان کے یہاں سود نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ نہ ثمن ہیں اور نہ کھائے جاتے ہیں۔

اصول سود کی علت (۱) جنس ایک ہو (۲) اور شمن بنے کی یا کھانے کی چیز ہو۔
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, part two, page 73, Book of Sales. The effective cause in it is measure with genus and weight with genus. (3) So if a measured thing is sold with its genus or a weighed thing with its genus, like for like, the sale is permissible; if they differ, it is not permissible. [Urdu: He can give two handfuls of cloth and take one. Or give one walnut and take two walnuts. Because nothing has been narrated in the hadiths regarding riba in counted or arm-length items. In the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that passed earlier, mention is made of dirham, dinar, and silver which are weighed, and wheat, barley, dates, and salt taken equally which are measured. Therefore, according to the Hanafis, riba occurs only if the item is weighed or measured. (1) The reason for making weight the cause is also indicated by this hadith: From Fadala ibn Ubaid, he said: We were with the Messenger of Allah on the day of Khaybar, selling gold ounces for two or three dinars, so the Messenger of Allah said: 'Do not sell gold for gold except weight for weight.' (Muslim) This hadith states 'weight for weight', indicating that riba occurs in weighed items. (2) In the hadith of Dar Qutni, it is explicitly stated that weighed and measured items are subject to riba: From Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab that the Messenger of Allah said: 'There is no riba except in gold or silver or in what is measured or weighed and is eaten or drunk.' (Dar Qutni) This mursal hadith explicitly states that gold, silver, or measured and weighed items that are eaten and drunk are subject to riba. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, the cause of riba is not measure and weight, but rather that there be one genus and thamaniyyah (monetary value) or food; then riba occurs. He says: In the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, gold and silver have thamaniyyah, i.e., the capacity to be price and value, and wheat, barley, dates, and salt are food, so thamaniyyah and food are the cause of riba. (2) In the hadith of Dar Qutni that passed, along with gold and silver, 'yukalu wa yushrabu' (measured and drunk) is specified, meaning that food is the cause of riba. Therefore, according to them, when the substance and price are the same thing, and that thing is either thaman or food, then riba occurs. So copper and iron are not subject to riba according to them, because they are not thaman nor eaten. The principle of the cause of riba: (1) the genus is the same, and (2) it is a thaman or a food item.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute on the effective cause ('illa) of riba. The author first states the Hanafi position: the 'illa is weight (wazn) or measure (kayl) combined with sameness of genus. He then cites hadith evidence: the hadith of Fadala ibn Ubaid emphasizing weight, and the hadith of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab explicitly mentioning weighed and measured items. Next, the Shafi'i position is presented: the 'illa is thamaniyyah (monetary value) for gold and silver, and food for the other items. The Shafi'i argument is that the six items in the hadith of Abu Sa'id are either thaman (gold, silver) or food (wheat, barley, dates, salt). The Dar Qutni hadith adds 'yukalu wa yushrabu' which they interpret as food. The author then gives the Hanafi response implicitly by showing that the explicit mention of weight and measure in the hadiths supports the Hanafi view. The practical difference: under Hanafi, items like copper and iron are ribawi if sold by weight; under Shafi'i, they are not. The passage concludes with the Hanafi summary of the 'illa: same genus and being thaman or food? Actually the summary restates the Hanafi position. The teacher should note that the dispute is fundamental and affects which goods are considered ribawi.

Key Terms
العلة (al-'illa): The effective cause that triggers the ruling of riba in a sale
الربوا (al-riba): Usurious increase in exchange of countervalues
الكيل (al-kayl): Measurement by volume
الوزن (al-wazn): Measurement by weight

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the effective cause of riba according to the Hanafi school as presented in this passage?
A) Thamaniyyah and food
B) Weight and measure with same genus
C) Edible and drinkable
D) All items sold by piece

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi 'illa of riba is weight or measure with genus identity, based on explicit hadith evidence.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Ruling on Selling Ribawi Items: Like-for-Like, Quality Disregarded, and the Permissible Stratagem
Rulings: like-for-like sale, no disparity, good vs poor quality, and exception when genus differs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on exchanging ribawi items of different quality, apply the like-for-like requirement, and construct the valid stratagem (hila) using currency.

Core Idea
In ribawi items, quality is irrelevant; only quantity equality matters or use currency as a medium.

This passage addresses a common transaction: exchanging one type of date for another of different quality. The Hanafi school clarifies that the prohibition of riba requires exact equality in quantity (weight or measure) when the genus is the same, regardless of quality differences. However, a practical stratagem using currency is provided to achieve a fair trade without violating the rule. The proof is a famous hadith from Abu Huraira.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Scope
Focus on the first sentence: 'لا يجوز بيع الجيد بالردى مما فيه الربوا الا مثلا بمثل'. This means selling good quality for poor quality in ribawi items is not allowed unless it is equal in quantity. Note the exception: if quantities are equal, the exchange is valid.
The ruling applies only to ribawi items (six known categories: gold, silver, wheat, barley, dates, salt) and by analogy to other measured/weighed items of the same genus.
2
Locate the Dalil – The Hadith of Abu Huraira
Read the hadith carefully. The Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade exchanging good dates (janeeb) for mixed dates (jam'a) with disparity and instructed: 'بع الجمع بالدراهم ثم ابتع بالدراهم جنيبا' – sell the mixed for dirhams, then buy good with dirhams.
The hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim, classified as ahad (single-chain), so zanni in transmission.
3
Derive the Wajh al-Dalalah (Proof Indication)
The Prophet's command 'لا تفعل' (do not do that) is a clear prohibition. The alternative method shows that the prohibition is tied to direct unequal exchange. The 'illa is the species and the 'meaning' (riba via weight/measure).
Hanafi usul: an absolute command implies prohibition (tahrim), and the stratagem demonstrates the intended flexibility.
4
Understand the Hila (Stratagem)
The hila is to sell the lower-quality item for dirhams (currency), then use the same dirhams to buy the higher-quality item from the same seller. This transforms the direct barter into two separate sales, each involving currency, thus avoiding riba.
The hila is valid because currency (gold/silver) is of a different genus (or same genus but different 'illa?) Actually dirhams and dates are different genera, so riba rules do not apply between them.
5
Recognize the Exception – When Disparity is Halal
The last sentence: if the two descriptors (genus and attached meaning) are not both present – meaning items are of different genera or not both ribawi – then disparity and credit are permissible.
This is the general principle of riba: restrictions only bind when genus is the same and both are measured/weighed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشرح الثميرى الجزء الثانى ۷۴ كتاب البيوع

[۹۳۵] (۴) ولا يجوز بيع الجيد بالردى مما فيه الربوا الا مثلا بمثل

جن چیزوں میں ربوا جاری ہوتا ہے مثلا گیہوں تو چاہے عمدہ گیہوں کو گھٹیا گیہوں کے بدلے میں بیچے پھر بھی برابر سرابر ہی بیچنا پڑے گا ور نہ سود ہو جائے گا۔

ان چیزوں میں عمدہ اور گھٹیا تو ہوتا ہی ہے۔ اسی لئے تو بیع کرتا ہے۔ پس اگر کمی بیشی جائز قرار دیدے تو ربوا کا دروازہ کھل جائے گا۔اس لئے ان میں صفت کے اعلی اور ادنی کا اعتبار نہیں ہے۔ برابر سرابر ہی بیچنا پڑے گا۔ اور اگر برابر سرابر نہیں بیچنا چاہتا ہے تو یوں کرے کہ مثلا گھٹیا کھجور ایک پونڈ کے دو کیلو مشتری کے ہاتھ بیچ دے اور اسی مشتری سے ایک پونڈ کا ایک کیلو عمدہ کھجور خرید لے۔ اس صورت میں کھجور کھجور کے بدلے میں نہیں ہوا بلکہ دو کیلو گھٹیا کھجور کے بدلے ایک پونڈ آیا اور ایک کیلوعمدہ کھجور ایک پونڈ کے بدلے لیا گیا۔ اس لئے پونڈ سے کھجور کی قیمت لگی اس لئے جائز ہو جائے گی (۲) حدیث میں عمدہ کھجور کوگھٹیا کھجور کے بدلے کمی بیشی کر کے بیچنے سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ اور کھجور کو درہم کے بدلے بیچنے کی صورت جتلائی ہے۔ عن ابی هریرة ان رسول الله الله الله استعمل رجلا على خيبر فـ فجائه بتمر جنيب فقال رسول الله اكل تمر خیبر هكذا؟ قال لا والله يا رسول الله انا لنأخذ الصاع من هذا بالصاعين والصاعين بالثلاث فقال رسول الله لا تفعل بع الجمع بالدراهم ثم ابتع بالدراهم جنيبا (ب) ( بخاری شریف ، باب اذا اراد بیع تمر بتمر خیر منہ ص ۲۹۳ نمبر ۲۰۱ ر مسلم شریف ، باب بیع الطعام مثلا بمثل ص ۲۴ نمبر ۴۰۸۲/۱۵۹۳) اس حدیث میں خیبر کے جنیب کھجور کو جمع کھجور کے بدلے کمی بیشی کر کے خریدا اور حضور کے سامنے لایا تو آپ نے منع فرمایا اور فرمایا کہ کھجور کو درہم کے بدلے بیچو پھر اس درہم سے عمدہ کھجور خرید لو۔ چاہے اسی مشتری سے کیوں نہ خرید و۔ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ربوی چیزوں میں عمدہ اور گھٹیا کا اعتبار نہیں ہے۔ برابر سرابر ہی بیچنا ہوگا ورنہ سود ہوگا۔

[۹۳۶] (۵) اگر دونوں وصف نہ ہوں یعنی جنس اور وہ معنی جو اس کے ساتھ ملائی گئی ہو تو کمی بیشی حلال ہے اور ادھار بھی حلال ہے۔
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, part two, page 74, Book of Sales. [935] (4) It is not permissible to sell good quality for poor quality in what involves riba except like for like. In items where riba applies, e.g., wheat, even if you sell good wheat for bad wheat, you must sell equal for equal; otherwise riba will occur. These items have quality difference, that is why one sells. So if disparity were permitted, the door of riba would open. Therefore, in these items, the characteristic of high or low is not considered; they must be sold equal for equal. And if one does not want to sell equal for equal, he should do this: for example, sell two kilograms of bad dates to the buyer for one pound, and from the same buyer buy one kilogram of good dates for one pound. In this case, dates are not exchanged for dates, but two kilograms of bad dates are exchanged for one pound, and one kilogram of good dates is taken for one pound. So the pound becomes the price of dates, thus it becomes permissible. (2) In the hadith, it is forbidden to sell good dates for bad dates with disparity, and the method of selling dates for dirhams is taught: From Abu Huraira that the Messenger of Allah appointed a man over Khaybar, and he brought good dates. The Prophet said: 'Are all dates of Khaybar like this?' He said: 'No, by Allah, we take a sa' of these for two sa's and two sa's for three.' The Prophet said: 'Do not do that. Sell the mixed dates for dirhams, then buy good dates with dirhams.' (Bukhari, Muslim) This hadith shows that good and bad quality are not considered in ribawi items; they must be sold equal for equal, otherwise riba occurs. [936] (5) If both descriptors are not present, i.e., the genus and the meaning that is attached to it, then disparity and credit are halal.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage contains two rulings. First (4): In ribawi items (e.g., wheat, dates), selling good quality for poor quality is not allowed even if the quantities are equal? Actually the ruling says it is not allowed except like for like. The commentary clarifies: even if quality differs, the exchange must be exactly equal in quantity (weight or measure). If disparity occurs, it is riba. The author then presents a legal stratagem (hila): to avoid direct exchange, sell the cheaper item for currency (e.g., pounds) and then use that currency to buy the better item. This circumvents the prohibition because currency is not of the same genus. The proof is the hadith of Abu Huraira where the Prophet prohibited direct unequal exchange of dates and prescribed the use of dirhams. Second ruling (5): If the two descriptors (genus and the attached meaning, i.e., the 'illa) are not both present—meaning the items are not of the same genus or not both ribawi—then disparity and credit are permissible. This is the general principle: riba restrictions only apply when genus is the same and the items are measured/weighed.

Key Terms
الجيد (al-jayyid): Good quality item in a ribawi genus
الردى (al-radi'): Poor quality item in a ribawi genus
مثلا بمثل (mithlan bi mithl): Equal in quantity (weight or measure)
الحيلة (al-hila): Legal stratagem to avoid riba

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited, what did the Prophet instruct the man from Khaybar to do when confronted with unequal exchange of dates?
A) Exchange an equal quantity of dates regardless of quality
B) Sell the mixed dates for dirhams, then buy good dates with dirhams
C) Add more dates to make the quantities equal
D) Return the dates and seek other food

Key Takeaway
In ribawi items, only quantity equality matters for the same genus; quality is irrelevant; use currency to bypass riba when quantities differ.
